In particular, note that the values in the private slot of  $\mathbf{u}$  are set to 0 and ict is generated using IPFE.SlotEnc (depicted as  $\bot$  in the private slot of  $\mathbf{u}$ ).
- <u>Hybrid  $H_1^b$ </u> proceeds identically to  $H_0^b$ , except that the IPFE ciphertext ict is generated using IPFE.Enc with values in the private slot set to 0. In Figure 4, the " $\bot$ " values in  $H_0^b$  change into 0 in  $H_1^b$ . By the *slot-mode* correctness of the slotted IPFE scheme,  $H_0^b$  and  $H_1^b$  are identically distributed.
- <u>Hybrid H</u><sup>b</sup><sub>2</sub> proceeds identically to H<sup>b</sup><sub>1</sub>, except that how the pad  $\overline{\mu}_q$  and labels  $\overline{L}_{q,j}(\mathbf{x})$  for  $q \in [Q], j \in [m_q]$  are computed (as inner products) is changed instead of combining k independent garblings (in the secret keys) with weights  $\mathbf{s}$  (in the ciphertext), we put the k independent garblings as well as their linear combinations in the secret keys and the ciphertext only uses that linear combination.

Recall that in  $\mathsf{H}_1^b$  (the same as in  $\mathsf{Exp}_{\mathrm{CPA}}^b$ ),  $\overline{\mu}_q$  and  $\overline{L}_{q,j}(\mathbf{x})$  are linear combinations of  $\{\boldsymbol{\mu}_q[t]\}_{t\in[k]}$  and  $\{L_{q,j}^t(\mathbf{x})\}_{t\in[k]}$  with weights  $\mathbf{s}\in\mathbb{Z}_p^k$ , which are computed using IPFE as these inner products:

$$\overline{\mu}_q = \langle \boldsymbol{\mu}_q, \mathbf{s} \rangle, 
\overline{L}_{q,j}(\mathbf{x}) = \langle \left( \mathbf{L}_{q,j}^1, \dots, \mathbf{L}_{q,j}^k \right), \left( \mathbf{s}[1](1, \mathbf{x}), \dots, \mathbf{s}[k](1, \mathbf{x}) \right) \rangle,$$

where the random multiples of the attribute  $(\mathbf{s}[1](1,\mathbf{x}),\ldots,\mathbf{s}[k](1,\mathbf{x}))$  are encoded in the public slot of  $\mathbf{u}$ ,  $\boldsymbol{\mu}_q$  in the public slots of  $\mathbf{v}_{q,\mathrm{pad}}$ , and the coefficients  $(\mathbf{L}_{q,j}^1,\ldots,\mathbf{L}_{q,j}^k)$  of the k label functions in the public slots of  $\mathbf{v}_{q,j}$ . In  $\mathsf{H}_2^b$ ,  $\overline{\mu}_q$  and  $\overline{L}_{q,j}(\mathbf{x})$  are instead computed as

$$\begin{split} \overline{\mu}_q &= \langle \overline{\mu}_q, 1 \rangle, \\ \overline{L}_{q,j}(\mathbf{x}) &= \langle \overline{\mathbf{L}}_{q,j}, (1, \mathbf{x}) \rangle, \quad \overline{\mathbf{L}}_{q,j} = \sum_{t \in [k]} \mathbf{s}[t] \mathbf{L}_{q,j}^t, \end{split}$$

where  $(1, \mathbf{x})$  is encoded in the *private* slot  $\mathbf{u}$ ,  $\overline{\mu}_q$  in the *private* slots of  $\mathbf{v}_{q,\text{pad}}$ , and  $\overline{\mathbf{L}}_{q,j}$  in the *private* slots of  $\mathbf{v}_{q,\text{pad}}$ . Furthermore, to keep the inner products  $\langle \mathbf{u}, \mathbf{v}_{q,\text{pad}} \rangle$  and  $\langle \mathbf{u}, \mathbf{v}_{q,j} \rangle$  the same as those in  $\mathsf{H}_1^b$ , the random multiples of the attribute  $(\mathbf{s}[1](1,\mathbf{x}),\ldots,\mathbf{s}[k](1,\mathbf{x}))$  in the *public* slot of  $\mathbf{u}$  are replaced by zero (while the public slots of  $\mathbf{v}_{q,\text{pad}},\mathbf{v}_{q,j}$  remain unchanged). By the function-hiding property of IPFE,  $\mathsf{H}_2^b$  is indistinguishable from  $\mathsf{H}_1^b$ .

<span id="page-41-0"></span>

| hybrid                              | vector                                              | pad                     | $const^t$                     | $coef_i^t$                                | const                                                                                    | $coef_i$                              | $sim_1, sim_\star$ |
|-------------------------------------|-----------------------------------------------------|-------------------------|-------------------------------|-------------------------------------------|------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|---------------------------------------|--------------------|
|                                     | $\boxed{sk_q\colon \mathbf{v}_{q,\mathrm{pad}}}$    | 1                       | $\boldsymbol{\mu}_q[t]$       | 0                                         | 0                                                                                        | 0                                     | 0                  |
| $H_0^b \equiv Exp_{\mathrm{CPA}}^b$ | $sk_q \colon \mathbf{v}_{q,j}$                      | 0                       | $\mathbf{L}_{q,j}^t[const]$   | $\mathbf{L}_{q,j}^t[coef_i]$              | 0                                                                                        | 0                                     | 0                  |
|                                     | $\begin{bmatrix} \bar{ct} \end{bmatrix}$ : <b>u</b> | h                       | $\mathbf{s}[t]$               | $\mathbf{s}[t]\mathbf{x}[i]$              |                                                                                          | $\perp$                               | Τ                  |
|                                     | $\boxed{sk_q \colon \mathbf{v}_{q,\mathrm{pad}}}$   | 1                       | $\boldsymbol{\mu}_q[t]$       | 0                                         | $\begin{bmatrix} 0 \end{bmatrix}$                                                        | 0                                     | 0                  |
| $H_1^b$                             | $sk_q \colon \mathbf{v}_{q,j}$                      | 0                       | $\mathbf{L}_{q,j}^t[const]$   | $\mathbf{L}_{q,j}^t[coef_i]$              | $\begin{bmatrix} 0 \end{bmatrix}$                                                        | $\begin{bmatrix} 0 \end{bmatrix}$     | 0                  |
|                                     | ct: u                                               | h                       | $\lceil \mathbf{s}[t] \rceil$ | $\left[\mathbf{s}[t]\mathbf{x}[i]\right]$ | $\begin{bmatrix} 0 \end{bmatrix}$                                                        | $\llbracket 0 \rceil$                 | 0                  |
|                                     | $sk_q \colon \mathbf{v}_{q,\mathrm{pad}}$           | 1                       | $\boldsymbol{\mu}_q[t]$       | 0                                         | $\overline{\mu}_q$                                                                       | 0                                     | 0                  |
| $H_2^b$                             | $sk_q \colon \mathbf{v}_{q,j}$                      | 0                       | $\mathbf{L}_{q,j}^t[const]$   | $\mathbf{L}_{q,j}^t[coef_i]$              | $\overline{\mathbf{L}}_{q,j}[const]$                                                     | $\overline{\mathbf{L}}_{q,j}[coef_i]$ | 0                  |
|                                     | ct: u                                               | h                       | 0                             | 0                                         | 1                                                                                        | $\boxed{\mathbf{x}[i]}$               | 0                  |
|                                     | $sk_q \colon \mathbf{v}_{q,\mathrm{pad}}$           | 1                       | $\boldsymbol{\mu}_q[t]$       | 0                                         | $\left[\widehat{\mu}_{q}\right]$                                                         | 0                                     | 0                  |
| $H_3^b \equiv H_{4,1}^b$            | $sk_q \colon \mathbf{v}_{q,j}$                      | 0                       | $\mathbf{L}_{q,j}^t[const]$   | $\mathbf{L}_{q,j}^t[coef_i]$              | $\widehat{\mathbf{L}}_{q,j}[const]$                                                      | $\widehat{\mathbf{L}}_{q,j}[coef_i]$  | 0                  |
|                                     | ct: u                                               | h                       | 0                             | 0                                         | 1                                                                                        | $\mathbf{x}[i]$                       | 0                  |
| $H^b_{4,1\sim Q+1}$                 |                                                     |                         |                               |                                           |                                                                                          |                                       |                    |
|                                     | $\boxed{sk_q \colon \mathbf{v}_{q,\mathrm{pad}}}$   | 1                       | $\boldsymbol{\mu}_q[t]$       | 0                                         | $\widehat{\mu}_q' \overset{\hspace{0.1em}\scriptscriptstyle\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_p$ | 0                                     | 0                  |
| $H^b_5 \equiv H^b_{4,Q+1}$          | $sk_q \colon \mathbf{v}_{q,j}$                      | 0                       | $\mathbf{L}_{q,j}^t[const]$   | $\mathbf{L}_{q,j}^t[coef_i]$              | $\widehat{\widehat{\mathbf{L}}}_{q,j}[const]$                                            | $\widehat{\mathbf{L}}_{q,j}[coef_i]$  | 0                  |
|                                     | ct: u                                               | $\boxed{\bar{\bar{L}}}$ | 0                             | 0                                         | 1                                                                                        | $\mathbf{x}[i]$                       | 0                  |
|                                     | $sk_q \colon \mathbf{v}_{q,\mathrm{pad}}$           | 1                       | $\boldsymbol{\mu}_q[t]$       | 0                                         | $h + \widehat{\mu}'_q$                                                                   | 0                                     | 0                  |
| $H_6^b$                             | $sk_q \colon \mathbf{v}_{q,j}$                      | 0                       | $\mathbf{L}_{q,j}^t[const]$   | $\mathbf{L}_{q,j}^t[coef_i]$              | $\widehat{\mathbf{L}}_{q,j}[const]$                                                      | $\widehat{\mathbf{L}}_{q,j}[coef_i]$  | 0                  |
|                                     | ct: u                                               | 0                       | 0                             | 0                                         | 1                                                                                        | $\mathbf{x}[i]$                       | 0                  |

The hybrids are illustrated with ciphertext challenge coming after the key queries (as in the more difficult case for 1-ABE). In reality, the key queries can be made before and after the ciphertext challenge, and the proof is unaffected.

Figure 4: The hybrids (with the loop contracted) in the proof of IND-CPA security of our KP-ABE scheme for ABPs.

In  $\mathsf{H}_2^b$ , the linearly combined  $\overline{\mathbf{L}}_{q,j} = \sum_{t \in [k]} \mathbf{s}[t] \mathbf{L}_{q,j}^t$  are valid garblings for the linearly combined pads  $\overline{\mu}_q = \langle \mathbf{s}, \boldsymbol{\mu}_q \rangle$ .

In  $\mathsf{H}_3^b$ , the garblings  $\widehat{\mathbf{L}}_{q,j}$  are fresh and are for freshly sampled pads  $\widehat{\mu}_q$ . In  $\mathsf{H}_5^b, \mathsf{H}_6^b$ , the pads  $\widehat{\mu}_q'$  in  $\mathsf{sk}_{q,\mathrm{pad}}$  are independent of the pads  $(\widehat{\mu}_q)$  being garbled.

• <u>Hybrid H</u><sup>b</sup><sub>3</sub> proceeds identically to H<sup>b</sup><sub>2</sub>, except that the random linear combinations  $\overline{\mu_q}$ ,  $\overline{\mathbf{L}}_{q,j}$  in the private slots of the secret keys are replaced by randomly and independently generated pads and garblings  $\widehat{\mu_q}$ ,  $\widehat{\mathbf{L}}_{q,j}$ , as shown in Figure 4.

Recall that in both hybrids, the k instances of garblings in the public slot are generated by

$$\begin{split} \boldsymbol{\mu}_{q} &\overset{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_{p}^{k}, \quad \boldsymbol{\eta}_{q} &\overset{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_{p}^{k}, \quad \begin{cases} \boldsymbol{\alpha}_{q} \leftarrow \boldsymbol{\mu}_{q}, \quad \boldsymbol{\beta}_{q} \leftarrow \mathbf{0}, & \text{if } y_{q} = f_{q, \neq 0}; \\ \boldsymbol{\alpha}_{q} \leftarrow \boldsymbol{\eta}_{q}, \quad \boldsymbol{\beta}_{q} \leftarrow \boldsymbol{\mu}_{q}, & \text{if } y_{q} = f_{q, = 0}; \end{cases} \\ \text{for } t \in [k] \colon \quad (\mathbf{L}_{q,1}^{t}, \dots, \mathbf{L}_{q,m_{q}}^{t}) = \mathsf{Garble}(f_{q}, \boldsymbol{\alpha}_{q}[t], \boldsymbol{\beta}_{q}[t]; \mathbf{r}_{q,t}). \end{split}$$

In  $H_2^b$ , the private slots of ABE secret keys contain linear combinations of the garblings. By the linearity of AKGS, they can also be generated as follows:

$$\begin{cases} \overline{\alpha}_q = \langle \mathbf{s}, \boldsymbol{\alpha}_q \rangle = \overline{\mu}_q = \langle \mathbf{s}, \boldsymbol{\mu}_q \rangle, & \overline{\beta}_q = \langle \mathbf{s}, \boldsymbol{\beta}_q \rangle = \ 0 = \langle \mathbf{s}, \mathbf{0} \rangle, & \text{if } y_q = f_{q, \neq 0}; \\ \overline{\alpha}_q = \langle \mathbf{s}, \boldsymbol{\alpha}_q \rangle = \overline{\eta}_q = \langle \mathbf{s}, \boldsymbol{\eta}_q \rangle, & \overline{\beta}_q = \langle \mathbf{s}, \boldsymbol{\beta}_q \rangle = \overline{\mu}_q = \langle \mathbf{s}, \boldsymbol{\mu}_q \rangle, & \text{if } y_q = f_{q, = 0}; \\ \overline{\mathbf{r}}_q = \sum_{t \in [k]} \mathbf{s}[t] \mathbf{r}_{q,t}, & (\overline{\mathbf{L}}_{q,1}, \dots, \overline{\mathbf{L}}_{q,m}) = \mathsf{Garble}(f_q, \overline{\alpha}_q, \overline{\beta}_q; \overline{\mathbf{r}}_q). \end{cases}$$

In  $\mathsf{H}_3^b$ ,  $\widehat{\mathbf{L}}_{q,j}$ 's are generated for randomly and independently sampled pad  $\widehat{\mu}_q$  with secrets  $\widehat{\alpha}_q$ ,  $\widehat{\beta}_q$  set according to  $\widehat{\mu}_q$  and independent randomness  $\widehat{\mathbf{r}}_q$ :

$$\begin{split} \widehat{\mu}_q & \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_p, \quad \widehat{\eta}_q & \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_p, \quad \begin{cases} \widehat{\alpha}_q \leftarrow \widehat{\mu}_q, \quad \widehat{\beta}_q \leftarrow 0, \qquad \text{if } y = f_{q, \neq 0}; \\ \widehat{\alpha}_q \leftarrow \widehat{\eta}_q, \quad \widehat{\beta}_q \leftarrow \widehat{\mu}_q, \qquad \text{if } y = f_{q, = 0}; \end{cases} \\ (\widehat{\mathbf{L}}_{q,1}, \dots, \widehat{\mathbf{L}}_{q,m}) &= \mathsf{Garble}(f_q, \widehat{\alpha}_q, \widehat{\beta}_q; \widehat{\mathbf{r}}_q). \end{split}$$

Note that the only difference between  $\mathsf{H}_2^b$  and  $\mathsf{H}_3^b$  is that the former uses linear combinations  $\overline{\mu}_q, \overline{\eta}_q, \overline{\mathbf{r}}_q$  to set the the secrets and the randomness for the garbling in the private slot. In contrast,  $\mathsf{H}_3^b$  uses fresh randomness. Note that in  $\mathsf{H}_2^b$ , the weights  $\mathbf{s}$  and  $\boldsymbol{\mu}_q, \boldsymbol{\eta}_q, \mathbf{r}_{q,t}$  are only used in the exponent of the second source group  $G_2$  (since they are only encoded in IPFE secret keys). Therefore, by the MDDH<sub>k</sub> assumption,  $\overline{\mu}_q, \overline{\eta}_q, \overline{\mathbf{r}}_q$  are pseudorandom in the exponent of  $G_2$ , i.e.,

$$\{ [\![\underline{\boldsymbol{\mu}_q, \boldsymbol{\eta}_q, \{\mathbf{r}_{q,t}\}_{t \in [k]}}, \underbrace{\overline{\boldsymbol{\mu}_q, \overline{\boldsymbol{\eta}}_q, \overline{\mathbf{r}}_q}}_{\mathbf{s}^\mathsf{T}\mathbf{A}}]\!]_2 \}_{q \in [Q]} \approx \{ [\![\boldsymbol{\mu}_q, \boldsymbol{\eta}_q, \{\mathbf{r}_{q,t}\}_{t \in [k]}, \underbrace{\widehat{\boldsymbol{\mu}_q, \widehat{\boldsymbol{\eta}}_q, \widehat{\mathbf{r}}_q}}_{\mathbf{c}^\mathsf{T}}]\!]_2 \}_{q \in [Q]}.$$

Furthermore, by the linearity of Garble, given these randomness encoded in  $G_2$ , the hybrids  $\mathsf{H}_2^b$  and  $\mathsf{H}_3^b$  can be efficiently generated. Thus, the two hybrids are indistinguishable.

We now have completed the first step of the proof. Observe that in  $\mathsf{H}_3^b$ , for each  $q \in [Q]$ , the private slots of  $\{\mathsf{isk}_{q,j}\}_{j\in[m_q]}$  encode (the coefficients of) label functions  $\widehat{L}_{q,j}$  and the private slot of ict encodes  $(1,\mathbf{x})$ , identical to that in the secret key and ciphertext of our 1-ABE scheme. The security of 1-ABE (Theorem 25) ensures that the adversary cannot distinguish the pad  $\widehat{\mu}_q$  encoded in the secret key from another independent pad  $\widehat{\mu}'_q$  (inconsistent with  $\widehat{L}_{q,j}$ 's). Next, in hybrids  $\mathsf{H}_{4,1}^b,\ldots,\mathsf{H}_{4,Q+1}^b$ , we use syntactically the same proof to gradually switch each  $\widehat{\mu}_q$  to  $\widehat{\mu}'_q$ .

• <u>Hybrid H</u><sup>b</sup><sub>4,q</sub> proceeds identically to H<sup>b</sup><sub>3</sub>, except that in the first q-1 secret keys, the random pads  $\widehat{\mu}_{q'}$  (q' < q) in the private slot of  $\mathbf{v}_{q',\mathrm{pad}}$  are replaced by an independent random value  $\widehat{\mu}'_{q'}$ , as illustrated in Figure 5. The only difference between H<sup>b</sup><sub>4,q</sub> and H<sup>b</sup><sub>4,q+1</sub> is whether  $\mathbf{v}_{q,\mathrm{pad}}$  contains the pad  $\widehat{\mu}_q$  consistent with  $\widehat{L}_{q,j}$ 's or an independent one  $\widehat{\mu}'_q$ .

<span id="page-43-0"></span>

| hybrid        | vector                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                           | $\mid$ in $\mathfrak{s}_{\text{pub}}$ | const                                                                                                                                    | $coef_i$                                                                | $sim_1, sim_\star$ |
|---------------|------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|---------------------------------------|------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|-------------------------------------------------------------------------|--------------------|
|               | $v_{q',\mathrm{pad}}$                                                                                                                                                                                                                                            |                                       | $\widehat{\mu}'_{q'} \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_p$                                                                             | 0                                                                       | 0                  |
|               | $q' < q \begin{cases} \mathbf{v}_{q', \text{pad}} \\ \mathbf{v}_{q', j} \end{cases}$                                                                                                                                                                             |                                       | $\widehat{\mathbf{L}}_{q',j} \overset{\hspace{0.1em}\scriptscriptstyle\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_p \ \widehat{\mathbf{L}}_{q',j}[const]$ | $\widehat{\mathbf{L}}_{q',j}[coef_i]$                                   | 0                  |
| $H_{4,q}^b$   | $sk_q \left\{\begin{array}{l} \mathbf{v}_{q,\mathrm{pad}} \ \mathbf{v}_{q,i} \end{array}\right.$                                                                                                                                                                 |                                       | $\bar{\widehat{\mu}_q}$                                                                                                                  |                                                                         | 0                  |
| $_{4,q}$      | $\big \big \mathbf{v}_{q,j}$                                                                                                                                                                                                                                     |                                       | $\widehat{\mathbf{L}}_{q,j}[const]$                                                                                                      | $\widehat{\mathbf{L}}_{q,j}[coef_i]$                                    | 0                  |
|               | $v_{q',pad}$                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                     |                                       | $\widehat{\mu}_{q'}$                                                                                                                     | 0                                                                       | 0                  |
|               |                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                  |                                       | $\widehat{\mathbf{L}}_{q',j}[const]$                                                                                                     | $\widehat{\mathbf{L}}_{q',j}[coef_i]$                                   | 0                  |
|               | ct: u                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                            | h, <b>0</b> , <b>0</b>                | 1                                                                                                                                        | $\mathbf{x}[i]$                                                         | 0                  |
|               | $V_{q',pad}$                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                     |                                       | $\widehat{\mu}'_{q'} \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_p$                                                                             | 0                                                                       | 0                  |
| $H^b_{4,q+1}$ | $q' < q \begin{cases} \mathbf{v}_{q', \mathrm{pad}} \\ \mathbf{v}_{q', j} \end{cases}$ $sk_q \begin{cases} \mathbf{v}_{q, \mathrm{pad}} \\ \mathbf{v}_{q, j} \end{cases}$ $q' > q \begin{cases} \mathbf{v}_{q', \mathrm{pad}} \\ \mathbf{v}_{q', j} \end{cases}$ | \$ 57                                 | $\widehat{\mathbf{L}}_{q',j}[coef_i]$                                                                                                    | 0                                                                       |                    |
|               |                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                  |                                       | $\widehat{\mu}_q' \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_p$                                                                                | 0                                                                       | 0                  |
|               |                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                  |                                       | $\widehat{\mathbf{L}}_{q,j}[const]$                                                                                                      | $\widehat{\mathbf{L}}_{q,j}[const]  \widehat{\mathbf{L}}_{q,j}[coef_i]$ |                    |
|               |                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                  |                                       | $\widehat{\mu}_{q'}$                                                                                                                     | 0                                                                       | 0                  |
|               |                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                  |                                       | $\widehat{\mathbf{L}}_{q',j}[const]$                                                                                                     | $\widehat{\mathbf{L}}_{q',j}[coef_i]$                                   | 0                  |
|               | ct: u                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                            | h, <b>0</b> , <b>0</b>                | 1                                                                                                                                        | $\mathbf{x}[i]$                                                         | 0                  |

The proof is unaffected by whether each sk appears before/after ct. The "normal" in  $\mathbf{v}|_{\mathfrak{F}_{\mathrm{pub}}}$  represents the values specified by the honest KeyGen (the same as in Figure 4).

The garblings  $\widehat{\mathbf{L}}_{q',j}$  are fresh and are for freshly sampled pads  $\widehat{\mu}_{q'}$ , and  $\widehat{\mu}'_{q'}$  are independent of them.

In this iteration,  $sk_q$  is made apparently useless for decrypting ct.

Figure 5: The loop hybrids in the proof of IND-CPA security of our KP-ABE scheme for ABPs.

The indistinguishability of  $\mathsf{H}^b_{4,q}$  and  $\mathsf{H}^b_{4,q+1}$  follows by syntactically the same proof of 1-ABE security (Theorem 25). Recall that the proof of 1-ABE goes through a sequence of hybrids where the coefficients of the label functions  $\widehat{L}_{q,j}$ 's are gradually removed from  $\mathbf{v}_{q,j}|_{\mathfrak{s}_{1-\mathrm{ABE}}}$  and replaced by a simulated label hardcoded in either  $\mathbf{v}_{q,j}[\mathsf{const}]$  (using  $\mathbf{u}[\mathsf{sim}_{\star}]$  as a relay) or  $\mathbf{u}[\mathsf{sim}_{1}]$ . Simulated labels are sampled randomly  $\ell_{q,j} \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_p$  for every j > 1, except that the first one is reversely sampled

$$\ell_{q,1} \overset{\hspace{0.1em}\mathsf{\scriptscriptstyle\$}}{\leftarrow} \mathsf{RevSamp}(f_q,\mathbf{x},\widehat{\alpha}_q f_q(\mathbf{x}) + \widehat{\beta}_q,\ell_{q,2},\ldots,\ell_{q,m_q}).$$

If decryption should fail,  $\widehat{\alpha}_q f_q(\mathbf{x}) + \widehat{\beta}_q$  perfectly hides  $\widehat{\mu}_q$ , and  $\widehat{\mu}_q$  can be switched to  $\widehat{\mu}'_q$ . The indistinguishability of neighboring hybrids follows either from the AKGS piecewise security or the function-hiding property of IPFE.

The only differences between 1-ABE security proof and  $\mathsf{H}^b_{4,q} / \mathsf{H}^b_{4,q+1}$  are that in the latter the IPFE secret keys and ciphertext encode vectors with additional public slots, and that there are many (namely, Q) ABE secret keys. These differences do not affect the application of AKGS piecewise security nor the function-hiding property of IPFE. First, the piecewise security of AKGS is information-theoretic — given that  $\widehat{L}_{q,j}$  is randomly generated and independent of the other variables in  $\mathsf{H}^b_{4,q}$  and  $\mathsf{H}^b_{4,q+1}$ , it still applies. Second, the hybrids in 1-ABE security proof only modify the values in  $\mathbf{v}_{q,j}|_{\mathfrak{S}_{1-ABE}}$  and  $\mathbf{u}[\mathsf{sim}_1], \mathbf{u}[\mathsf{sim}_\star]$ , all of which are in the private slot. Moreover, the vectors  $\mathbf{v}_{q',j}, \mathbf{v}_{q',\text{pad}}$  in the additional secret keys (for  $q' \neq q$ ) have values at  $\mathsf{sim}_1, \mathsf{sim}_\star$  set to zero, and cannot "detect" the changes in  $\mathbf{u}[\mathsf{sim}_1], \mathbf{u}[\mathsf{sim}_\star]$ . Hence, all the inner products are kept the same and the function-hiding property of IPFE still applies. Therefore,  $\mathsf{H}^b_{4,q}$  and  $\mathsf{H}^b_{4,q+1}$  are indistinguishable.

We now have completed the second step of the proof. Observe that  $\mathsf{H}_3^b$  and  $\mathsf{H}_{4,1}^b$  are identical. We need another invocation of the function-hiding property of IPFE to remove h from  $\mathbf{u}$  (in ict):

• <u>Hybrid H</u><sup>b</sup><sub>5</sub> proceeds identically to H<sup>b</sup><sub>3</sub>, except that all the pads  $\widehat{\mu}_q$  in  $\mathbf{v}_{q,\mathrm{pad}}$ 's are replaced by independent random values  $\widehat{\mu}'_q$ , as illustrated in Figure 4. Observe that H<sup>b</sup><sub>4,Q+1</sub>  $\equiv$  H<sup>b</sup><sub>5</sub>, i.e., the loop hybrids connect H<sup>b</sup><sub>3</sub> and H<sup>b</sup><sub>5</sub>.

Note that in this hybrid, the inner products of  $\mathbf{u}$  and  $\mathbf{v}_{q,\mathrm{pad}}$ 's are  $h + \widehat{\mu}'_q$ , which hide h. However, h still appears in  $\mathbf{u}$ . In the next hybrid, we remove h from  $\mathbf{u}$  and directly hardwire the inner products  $h + \widehat{\mu}'_q$  in  $\mathbf{v}_{q,\mathrm{pad}}$ 's so that h becomes information-theoretically hidden.

• <u>Hybrid H</u><sup>b</sup><sub>6</sub> proceeds identically to H<sup>b</sup><sub>5</sub>, except that the pads h and  $\widehat{\mu}'_q$  are removed from **u**[pad] and  $\mathbf{v}_{q,\mathrm{pad}}[\mathrm{const}]$  respectively, and that their sums  $h + \widehat{\mu}'_q$  are put in  $\mathbf{v}_{q,\mathrm{pad}}[\mathrm{const}]$ . The change is illustrated in Figure 4. Since the inner products remain the same as in H<sup>b</sup><sub>5</sub>, by the function-hiding property of IPFE, H<sup>b</sup><sub>5</sub> and H<sup>b</sup><sub>6</sub> are indistinguishable.

Finally, we argue that  $\mathsf{H}_6^0 \equiv \mathsf{H}_6^1$ : The secret keys are independent of h since each  $\widehat{\mu}_q$  perfectly hides h. The only other place where h appears is for hiding the message:  $g_b + [\![h]\!]_T$  in ct. This means  $g_b$  is information-theoretically hidden by h.

By a hybrid argument, we have  $\mathsf{Exp}^0_{\mathsf{CPA}} \approx \mathsf{Exp}^1_{\mathsf{CPA}}$ , i.e., Construction 26 is IND-CPA secure.  $\square$ 

Combining Theorems 22 and 27, we obtain compact and adaptively secure ABE for ABP:

Corollary 28. Assuming  $MDDH_k$  in pairing groups, there is a compact and adaptively secure KP-ABE for ABP.

## <span id="page-45-0"></span>7 ABE for Uniform Logspace Turing Machines

In this section, we construct a KP-ABE scheme for L, uniform deterministic log-space computation. Here, each secret key is associated with a Turing machine M (with an arbitrary number of states Q), and each ciphertext is associated with an input  $\mathbf{x}$  (of arbitrary length N) and time/space complexity bounds  $T, S \geq 1$ . Decryption succeeds if and only if M accepts  $\mathbf{x}$  within time T and space S. More formally, the scheme handles a single predicate P:

$$X = \{(\mathbf{x}, 1^T, 1^{2^S}) \mid \mathbf{x} \in \{0, 1\}^N \text{ for some } N \ge 1, T, S \ge 1\}, \quad Y = \mathsf{TM},$$

$$P : X \times Y \to \{0, 1\}, \ \left((\mathbf{x}, 1^T, 1^{2^S}), M\right) \mapsto M|_{N, T, S}(\mathbf{x}) \text{ for } \mathbf{x} \in \{0, 1\}^N,$$

where  $M|_{N,T,S}$  (Definition 12) indicates whether M accepts  $\mathbf{x}$  within time T and space S. In our scheme, the size of a secret key is linear in Q and the size of a ciphertext is linear in  $TNS2^S$ .

Given our construction of ABE for L, we can derive ABE for DFA as a special case, since DFA can be viewed as a Turing machine with time complexity T=N and space complexity S=1, which always moves the input tape pointer to the right and never uses the work tape. Moreover, our ABE scheme for L extends immediately to non-deterministic, unambiguous logspace Turing machines (the complexity class UL). Such machines have at most one accepting path for any input. In fact, our construction handles all non-deterministic logspace Turing machines (the class NL), except when the number of accepting paths is exactly a multiple of p, the order of the pairing groups.

Below, we start with our AKGS for Turing machines, then build a 1-ABE scheme based on the AKGS and a function-hiding secret-key IPFE, and lastly lift it to a full-fledged KP-ABE scheme using slotted IPFE. For simplicity of exposition, we describe our construction based on the SXDH assumption in the pairing groups. It readily extends to be based on the MDDH<sub>k</sub> assumption for any  $k \geq 1$ .

### <span id="page-45-1"></span>7.1 AKGS for Turing Machines with Time/Space Bounds

To obtain our AKGS for Turing machines with time/space bounds, we first represent the computation of Turing machines as a sequence of matrix multiplications, and then design an AKGS for matrix multiplication. See Section 2.3 for an overview of our AKGS.

**Transition Matrix.** Given a Turing machine  $M = (Q, \mathbf{y}_{\text{acc}}, \delta)$ , upper bounds of time and space complexity  $T, S \geq 1$ , and an input  $\mathbf{x} \in \{0,1\}^N$  for some  $N \geq 1$ , we consider the length-T computation path of M with input  $\mathbf{x}$  and space bound S. Recall that the set of internal configurations is

$$C_{M,N,S} = [N] \times [S] \times \{0,1\}^S \times [Q].$$

An internal configuration  $z = (i, j, \mathbf{W}, q) \in \mathcal{C}_{M,N,S}$  specifies that the input and work tape pointers are at positions i and j respectively, the work tape has content  $\mathbf{W}$ , and the current state is q. In particular, the initial configuration is  $(1, 1, \mathbf{0}_S, 1)$ : the input/work tape pointers point to the first cell, the work tape is all-0, and the state is the initial state 1. An accepting configuration satisfies that  $\mathbf{y}_{acc}[q] = 1$ .

We construct a transition matrix  $\mathbf{M}_{N,S}(\mathbf{x}) \in \{0,1\}^{\mathcal{C}_{M,N,S} \times \mathcal{C}_{M,N,S}}$  such that  $\mathbf{M}_{N,S}(\mathbf{x})[z,z']$  is 1 if and only if the internal configuration of M is z' after 1 step of computation starting from internal configuration z. According to how the Turing machine operates in each step depending on the

transition function  $\delta$ , the entries of  $\mathbf{M}_{N,S}$  are defined as follows:

$$\begin{split} \mathbf{M}_{N,S}(\mathbf{x})[(i,j,\mathbf{W},q),(i',j',\mathbf{W}',q')] &= \begin{cases} 1, & \text{if } \delta(q,\mathbf{x}[i],\mathbf{W}[j]) = (q',\mathbf{W}'[j],i'-i,j'-j) \\ & \text{and } \mathbf{W}'[j''] = \mathbf{W}[j''] \text{ for all } j'' \neq j; \\ 0, & \text{otherwise}; \end{cases} \\ &= \mathbf{x}[i] \times \begin{cases} 1, & \text{if } \delta(q,1,\mathbf{W}[j]) = (q',\mathbf{W}'[j],i'-i,j'-j) \\ & \text{and } \mathbf{W}'[j''] = \mathbf{W}[j''] \text{ for all } j'' \neq j; \\ 0, & \text{otherwise}; \end{cases} \\ &(1-\mathbf{x}[i]) \times \begin{cases} 1, & \text{if } \delta(q,0,\mathbf{W}[j]) = (q',\mathbf{W}'[j],i'-i,j'-j) \\ & \text{and } \mathbf{W}'[j''] = \mathbf{W}[j''] \text{ for all } j'' \neq j; \\ 0, & \text{otherwise}. \end{cases} \end{split}$$

With the transition matrix, we can now write the computation of Turing machine as a sequence of matrix multiplication. We represent internal configurations using one-hot encoding — the internal configuration z is represented by the basis vector  $\mathbf{e}_z \in \{0,1\}^{C_{M,N,S}}$  whose z-entry is 1 and other entries are 0. Observe that multiplying  $\mathbf{e}_z^{\mathsf{T}}$  on the right by the transition matrix  $\mathbf{M}_{N,S}(\mathbf{x})$  produces exactly the next internal configuration: If there is no valid internal configuration of M after 1 step of computation starting from z, we have  $\mathbf{e}_z^{\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{M}_{N,S}(\mathbf{x}) = \mathbf{0}$ ; otherwise, the next internal configuration z' is unique and  $\mathbf{e}_z^{\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{M}_{N,S}(\mathbf{x}) = \mathbf{e}_z^{\mathsf{T}}$ . The function  $M|_{N,T,S}(\mathbf{x})$  can be written as

$$M|_{N,T,S}(\mathbf{x}) = \mathbf{e}_{(1,1,\mathbf{0}_S,1)}^{\mathsf{T}} \big( \mathbf{M}_{N,S}(\mathbf{x}) \big)^T \big( \mathbf{1}_{[N] \times [S] \times \{0,1\}^S} \otimes \mathbf{y}_{\mathrm{acc}} \big),$$

where  $\mathbf{e}_{(1,1,\mathbf{0}_S,1)}$  represents the initial internal configuration. The sequence of multiplication advances the computation by T steps and tests whether the final internal configuration is in an accepting state. We elaborate on the last step: The tensor product  $\mathbf{1}_{[N]\times[S]\times\{0,1\}^S}\otimes\mathbf{y}_{\mathrm{acc}}$  is a vector in  $\{0,1\}^{\mathcal{C}_{M,N,S}}$  such that its  $(i,j,\mathbf{W},q)$ -entry is 1 if and only if  $\mathbf{y}_{\mathrm{acc}}[q]=1$ , i.e., q is an accepting state. Therefore, taking the inner product of  $\mathbf{e}_{(1,1,\mathbf{0}_S,1)}^{\mathsf{T}}(\mathbf{M}_{N,S}(\mathbf{x}))^T=\mathbf{e}_{z'}^{\mathsf{T}}$  (z' is the final internal configuration) or  $\mathbf{0}$  with the tensor product indicates whether M accepts  $\mathbf{x}$  within time T and space S.

**Transition Blocks.** We observe that the transition matrix has the following two useful properties:

- $\mathbf{M}_{N,S}(\mathbf{x})$  is affine in  $\mathbf{x}$  when regarded as an integer matrix.
- $\mathbf{M}_{N,S}(\mathbf{x})$  has the following block structure: There is a finite set  $\{\mathbf{M}_{\tau}\}_{\tau}$  of  $Q \times Q$  matrices defined by the transition function  $\delta$ , called the *transition blocks*, such that for every  $(i, j, \mathbf{W})$  and  $(i', j', \mathbf{W}')$  in  $[N] \times [S] \times \{0, 1\}^S$ , the submatrix  $\mathbf{M}_{N,S}(\mathbf{x})[(i, j, \mathbf{W}, \square), (i', j', \mathbf{W}', \square)]$  is either some  $\mathbf{M}_{\tau}$  or  $\mathbf{0}$ .

We define the transition blocks below.

**Definition 29.** Let  $M = (Q, \mathbf{y}_{acc}, \delta)$  be a Turing machine and  $\mathcal{T} = \{0, 1\}^3 \times \{0, \pm 1\}^2$  the set of transition types. The transition blocks of M consist of 72 matrices  $\mathbf{M}_{\tau} \in \{0, 1\}^{Q \times Q}$  for  $\tau = (x, w, w', \Delta i, \Delta j) \in \mathcal{T}$ , each encoding the possible transitions among the states given the following information: the input tape symbol x under scan, the work tape symbol x under scan, the symbol x overwriting x, the direction x to which the input tape pointer moves, and the direction x to which the work tape pointer moves. Formally,

$$\mathbf{M}_{x,w,w',\Delta i,\Delta j}[q,q'] = \begin{cases} 1, & \text{if } \delta(q,x,w) = (q',w',\Delta i,\Delta j); \\ 0, & \text{otherwise.} \end{cases}$$

In  $\mathbf{M}_{N,S}(\mathbf{x})$ , each  $Q \times Q$  block is either one of the transition blocks or **0**:

$$\mathbf{M}_{N,S}(\mathbf{x})[(i,j,\mathbf{W},\llcorner),(i',j',\mathbf{W}',\llcorner)] = \begin{cases} \mathbf{M}_{\mathbf{x}[i],\mathbf{W}[j],\mathbf{W}'[j],i'-i,j'-j}, & \text{if } i'-i,j'-j \in \{0,\pm 1\} \text{ and} \\ & \mathbf{W}[j''] = \mathbf{W}'[j''] \text{ for all } j'' \neq j; \\ \mathbf{0}, & \text{otherwise.} \end{cases}$$

Observe further that in  $\mathbf{M}_{N,S}(\mathbf{x})[(i,j,\mathbf{W},\square),(\square,\square,\square,\square)]$ , each transition block appears at most once.

**AKGS** for Turing machines. Above, we have represented the Turing machine computation as a sequence of matrix multiplication *over the integers*:

$$M|_{N,T,S}(\mathbf{x}) = \mathbf{e}_{(1,1,\mathbf{0}_S,1)}^{\mathsf{T}} \left( \mathbf{M}_{N,S}(\mathbf{x}) \right)^{T} \left( \mathbf{1}_{[N] \times [S] \times \{0,1\}^{S}} \otimes \mathbf{y}_{\mathrm{acc}} \right) \quad \text{for } \mathbf{x} \in \{0,1\}^{N}.$$
 (7)

We can formally extend <sup>13</sup>  $M|_{N,T,S}: \{0,1\}^N \to \{0,1\}$  to a  $\mathbb{Z}_p^N \to \mathbb{Z}_p$  function using the same matrix multiplication formula, preserving its behavior when the input comes from  $\{0,1\}^N$ . When p is clear from the context, we use  $M|_{N,T,S}$  to represent its extension over  $\mathbb{Z}_p$ .

We now construct an AKGS for Turing machine computations and prove its special piecewise security. It is constructed via a recursive mechanism for garbling matrix multiplications, which is inspired <sup>14</sup> by the garbling scheme for arithmetic NC<sup>1</sup> circuits in [AIK11] and the garbling mechanism for multiplication gates in [BGG<sup>+</sup>14].

<span id="page-47-2"></span>Construction 30 (AKGS for  $M|_{N,T,S}$ ). Let

$$\mathcal{F} = \left\{ M|_{N,T,S} : \mathbb{Z}_p^N \to \mathbb{Z}_p \,\middle|\, M \in \mathsf{TM},\, N,T,S \geq 1,\, p \text{ prime} \right\}$$

be the set of time/space bounded Turing machine computations. The AKGS (Garble, Eval) for the function class  $\mathcal{F}$  operates as follows:

• Garble  $((M, 1^N, 1^T, 1^{2^S}, p), \alpha, \beta)$  takes a function  $M|_{N,T,S}$  over  $\mathbb{Z}_p$  from  $\mathcal{F}$  and two secrets  $\alpha, \beta \in \mathbb{Z}_p$  as input. Suppose  $M = (Q, \mathbf{y}_{acc}, \delta)$ , the algorithm samples  $\mathbf{r}$  as the randomness by

for 
$$t \in [0..T]$$
:  $\mathbf{r}_t \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_p^{\mathcal{C}_{M,N,S}} \left( \mathcal{C}_{M,N,S} = [N] \times [S] \times \{0,1\}^S \times [Q] \right),$   
 $\mathbf{r} \in \mathbb{Z}_p^{[0..T] \times \mathcal{C}_{M,N,S}}, \quad \mathbf{r}[(t,i,j,\mathbf{W},q)] = \mathbf{r}_t[(i,j,\mathbf{W},q)].$ 

It computes the transition matrix  $\mathbf{M}_{N,S}(\mathbf{x})$  as a function of  $\mathbf{x}$  and defines the label functions by

$$L_{\text{init}}(\mathbf{x}) = \beta + \mathbf{e}_{(1,1,\mathbf{0}_S,1)}^{\mathsf{T}} \mathbf{r}_0,$$
for  $t \in [T]$ :  $(L_{t,z}(\mathbf{x}))_{z \in \mathcal{C}_{M,N,S}} = -\mathbf{r}_{t-1} + \mathbf{M}_{N,S}(\mathbf{x})\mathbf{r}_t,$ 

$$(L_{T+1,z}(\mathbf{x}))_{z \in \mathcal{C}_{M,N,S}} = -\mathbf{r}_T + \alpha \mathbf{1}_{[N] \times [S] \times \{0,1\}^S} \otimes \mathbf{y}_{\text{acc}}.$$

It collects the coefficients of these label functions and returns them.

Note: We show Garble satisfies the required properties of a linear AKGS (Definitions 13 and 14):

<span id="page-47-1"></span><span id="page-47-0"></span><sup>&</sup>lt;sup>13</sup>This is done to arithmetize the computation, adhering to the formalism of AKGS.

<sup>&</sup>lt;sup>14</sup>As a historical fact, the authors first came up with the AKGS for arithmetic formulae, abstracted out piecewise security, and only verified that the PGS for ABPs [IW14] is also a piecewise secure AKGS.

- The label functions are affine in x: Linit and L<sup>T</sup> +1,z for all z ∈ CM,N,S are constant with respect to x. The rest are Lt,z(x) = −rt−<sup>1</sup> + MN,S(x)r<sup>t</sup> [z]. Since MN,S(x) is affine in x and rt−1, r<sup>t</sup> are constant with respect to x, these label functions are also affine in x.
- Shape determinism holds: holds: The garbling size of M|N,T,S is 1 + (T + 1)NS2 <sup>S</sup>Q.
- Garble is linear in (α, β, r), i.e., the coefficients of the label functions are linear in (α, β, r). Observe that MN,S(x), e(1,1,0S,1) and yacc are constant with respect to (α, β, r), and α, β and r<sup>t</sup> for all t ∈ [0..T] are linear in (α, β, r). By the definition of the label functions, their coefficients are linear in (α, β, r).
- Eval (M, 1 <sup>N</sup> , 1 T , 1 2 S , p), x, `init,(`t,z)t∈[<sup>T</sup> +1],z∈CM,N,S takes a function M|N,T,S over Z<sup>p</sup> from F, an input string x ∈ Z N <sup>p</sup> and the labels as input. It first computes the transition matrix MN,S(x) with x substituted into it and sets `<sup>t</sup> = (`t,z)z∈CM,N,S for t ∈ [T + 1]. The algorithm computes and returns

$$\ell_{\text{init}} + \mathbf{e}_{(1,1,\mathbf{0}_S,1)}^{\mathsf{T}} \sum_{t=1}^{T+1} \left(\mathbf{M}_{N,S}(\mathbf{x})\right)^{t-1} \boldsymbol{\ell}_t.$$

Note: We show the correctness of the scheme. Plugging `t,z = Lt,z(x) and the formula for M|N,T,S into the summation, we find that it is a telescoping sum:

$$\mathbf{e}_{(1,1,\mathbf{0}_{S},1)}^{\mathsf{T}+1} \left( \mathbf{M}_{N,S}(\mathbf{x}) \right)^{t-1} \boldsymbol{\ell}_{t} = \mathbf{e}_{(1,1,\mathbf{0}_{S},1)}^{\mathsf{T}} \sum_{t=1}^{T} \left( \mathbf{M}_{N,S}(\mathbf{x}) \right)^{t-1} \left( -\mathbf{r}_{t-1} + \mathbf{M}_{N,S}(\mathbf{x}) \mathbf{r}_{t} \right)$$

$$+ \mathbf{e}_{(1,1,\mathbf{0}_{S},1)}^{\mathsf{T}} \left( \mathbf{M}_{N,S}(\mathbf{x}) \right)^{T} \left( -\mathbf{r}_{T} + \alpha \mathbf{1}_{[N] \times [S] \times \{0,1\}^{S}} \otimes \mathbf{y}_{\mathrm{acc}} \right)$$

$$= \mathbf{e}_{(1,1,\mathbf{0}_{S},1)}^{\mathsf{T}} \sum_{t=1}^{T} \left( -\left( \mathbf{M}_{N,S}(\mathbf{x}) \right)^{t-1} \mathbf{r}_{t-1} + \left( \mathbf{M}_{N,S}(\mathbf{x}) \right)^{t} \mathbf{r}_{t} \right)$$

$$- \mathbf{e}_{(1,1,\mathbf{0}_{S},1)}^{\mathsf{T}} \left( \mathbf{M}_{N,S}(\mathbf{x}) \right)^{T} \mathbf{r}_{T} + \alpha M|_{N,T,S}(\mathbf{x})$$

$$= -\mathbf{e}_{(1,1,\mathbf{0}_{S},1)}^{\mathsf{T}} \mathbf{r}_{0} + \alpha M|_{N,T,S}(\mathbf{x}).$$

The value returned by Eval is

$$\ell_{\text{init}} + \mathbf{e}_{(1,1,\mathbf{0}_S,1)}^{\mathsf{T}} \sum_{t=1}^{T+1} \left( \mathbf{M}_{N,S}(\mathbf{x}) \right)^{t-1} \boldsymbol{\ell}_t = \left( \beta + \mathbf{e}_{(1,1,\mathbf{0}_S,1)}^{\mathsf{T}} \mathbf{r}_0 \right) + \left( -\mathbf{e}_{(1,1,\mathbf{0}_S,1)}^{\mathsf{T}} \mathbf{r}_0 + \alpha M|_{N,T,S}(\mathbf{x}) \right)$$
$$= \beta + \alpha M|_{N,T,S}(\mathbf{x}).$$

Therefore, the scheme is correct. Moreover, Eval is linear in the labels, as seen from the formula of Eval.

<span id="page-48-0"></span>Theorem 31. Construction [30](#page-47-2) is special piecewise secure. More specifically, the label functions are ordered as Linit,(L1,z)z∈CM,N,S ,(L2,z)z∈CM,N,S , . . . ,(L<sup>T</sup> +1,z)z∈CM,N,S , the randomness is ordered as r0, r1, . . . , r<sup>T</sup> , and the randomizer of Lt,z is rt−1[z]. For each t ∈ [T + 1], the ordering of the components in (Lt,z)z∈CM,N,S and rt−<sup>1</sup> can be arbitrary, as long as the two are consistent.

Proof. By definition, the coefficient of `init in Eval is 1 6= 0. Now we prove the marginal randomness property. Recall that all the other label functions are grouped by time step t ∈ [T + 1]:

for 
$$t \in [T]$$
:  $(L_{t,z}(\mathbf{x}))_{z \in \mathcal{C}_{M,N,S}} = -\mathbf{r}_{t-1} + \mathbf{M}_{N,S}(\mathbf{x})\mathbf{r}_t$ ,  
 $(L_{T+1,z}(\mathbf{x}))_{z \in \mathcal{C}_{M,N,S}} = -\mathbf{r}_T + \alpha \mathbf{1}_{[N] \times [S] \times \{0,1\}^S} \otimes \mathbf{y}_{acc}$ .

Fix a group  $t \in [T+1]$  of the label functions. Each  $L_{t,z}$  (for  $z \in \mathcal{C}_{M,N,S}$ ), aside from  $\mathbf{r}_{t-1}[z]$  (which is in the constant), only uses components in  $\mathbf{r}_t$  (if  $t \leq T$ ) as randomness. Moreover, all the label functions in groups  $t+1, t+2, \ldots, T+1$  only use components in  $\mathbf{r}_t, \mathbf{r}_{t+1}, \ldots, \mathbf{r}_T$  as randomness. Therefore, all those label functions are in the special form, the randomizer of  $L_{t,z}$  is  $\mathbf{r}_{t-1}[z]$ , and the components in each group of  $L_{t,z}$ 's and  $\mathbf{r}_{t-1}$  can be reordered as long as they are consistent.  $\square$ 

#### <span id="page-49-0"></span>7.2 1-ABE for **L**

With the AKGS for Turing machines, we are ready to construct our 1-ABE for L and prove its security. To focus on the core idea, we present our construction assuming SXDH in the pairing groups and briefly discuss how to generalize the construction to be based on MDDH<sub>k</sub> for any  $k \geq 1$ .

New Challenge. As discussed in the technical overview (see Section 2.3), building ABE for L from AKGS faces new challenges comparing with ABE for ABPs. In particular, the size of the AKGS garbling is roughly  $TNS2^SQ$ . While the key generation algorithm knows Q and the encryption algorithms knows N, T, S, neither of them alone has full information of the size of the AKGS garbling. Furthermore, the total size of a pair of secret key and ciphertext is way smaller than the garbling size. Therefore, it is impossible to encode the label functions of AKGS in either the secret key or the ciphertext (in contrast, in ABE for ABPs, the label functions are completely encoded in the secret key). To overcome this challenge, we will i) let the secret key and ciphertext jointly generate the label functions, and ii) use pseudorandomness in the exponent.

An Exercise of Algebra. Recall that the AKGS for L samples randomness  $\mathbf{r} \in \mathbb{Z}_p^{[0..T] \times \mathcal{C}_{M,N,S}}$ . We will use "structured" elements  $\mathbf{r} = \mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}} \otimes \mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{f}}$  for  $\mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}} \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_p^{[0..T] \times [N] \times [S] \times \{0,1\}^S}$  and  $\mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{f}} \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_p^Q$  as the randomness for the AKGS garbling. Before laying out the construction, we first show that  $\mathbf{M}_{N,S}(\mathbf{x})\mathbf{r}_t$  (a central part of the label functions) can be expressed as a bilinear function of  $\mathbf{x}, \mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}}, \mathbf{x} \otimes \mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}}$  (known at encryption time) and  $\mathbf{M}_{\tau}\mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{f}}, \mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{f}}$ 's (known at key generation time), and hence can be computed as the inner products of vectors depending on these two groups of variables separately.

By our choice of randomness,  $\mathbf{r}_t = \mathbf{r}[t, \underline{\ }, \underline{\ }, \underline{\ }, \underline{\ }]$  is a block vector with each block being a multiple of  $\mathbf{r}_f$ . More precisely,  $\mathbf{r}_t[i,j,\mathbf{W},\underline{\ }] = \mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}}[(t,i,j,\mathbf{W})]\mathbf{r}_f$ . We compute each block of the product  $\mathbf{M}_{N,S}(\mathbf{x})\mathbf{r}_t$ :

Recall that in  $\mathbf{M}_{N,S}(\mathbf{x})[(i,j,\mathbf{W},\square),(\square,\square,\square,\square)]$ , each transition block appears at most once, and the other  $Q \times Q$  blocks are **0**. More specifically,  $\mathbf{M}_{x,w,w',\Delta i,\Delta j}$  appears at  $\mathbf{M}_{N,S}(\mathbf{x})[(i,j,\mathbf{W},\square),(i',j',\mathbf{W}',\square)]$  if  $x = \mathbf{x}[i], \ w = \mathbf{W}[j], \ \Delta i = i' - i, \ \Delta j = j' - j, \ \text{and} \ \mathbf{W}'$  is  $\mathbf{W}$  with its  $j^{\text{th}}$  entry changed to w'.

Therefore, we have

<span id="page-50-0"></span>
$$(\mathbf{M}_{N,S}(\mathbf{x})\mathbf{r}_{t})[(i,j,\mathbf{W},\square)] = \sum_{\substack{w' \in \{0,1\}\\ \Delta i, \Delta j \in \{0,\pm1\}\\ i+\Delta j \in [N], j+\Delta j \in [S]}} \mathbf{M}_{\mathbf{x}[i],\mathbf{W}[j],w',\Delta i,\Delta j} \mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}}[(t,i+\Delta i,j+\Delta j,\mathbf{W}')]\mathbf{r}_{f}$$

$$= \sum_{\substack{x,w,w' \in \{0,1\}\\ x,w,w' \in \{0,1\}}} \mathbf{M}_{x,w,w',\Delta i,\Delta j} \mathbf{r}_{f} \times \begin{cases} \mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}}[(t,i+\Delta i,j+\Delta j,\mathbf{W}')], & \text{if } x = \mathbf{x}[i], i+\Delta i \in [N],\\ w = \mathbf{W}[j], j+\Delta j \in [S];\\ 0, & \text{otherwise.} \end{cases}$$
(8)

Here,  $\mathbf{W}'[j] = w'$  and  $\mathbf{W}'[j''] = \mathbf{W}[j'']$  for all  $j'' \neq j$ . Note that in the last summation formula, there are exactly 72 summands. Moreover, each summand is  $\mathbf{M}_{x,w,w',\Delta i,\Delta j}\mathbf{r}_{\mathrm{f}}$  (depending only on  $\mathbf{r}_{\mathrm{f}}$  and the transition blocks) multiplied by an entry in  $\mathbf{r}_{\mathrm{x}}$  or 0 (depending only on  $\mathbf{x}, \mathbf{r}_{\mathrm{x}}$ ). To simplify notations, we define *transition coefficients*:

**Definition 32.** Let  $\mathcal{T} = \{0,1\}^3 \times \{0,\pm 1\}^2$  be the set of transition types. For all  $\tau = (x, w, w', \Delta i, \Delta j) \in \mathcal{T}$ ,  $N, T, S \geq 1$ , and  $\mathbf{x} \in \{0,1\}^N$ ,  $t \in [T]$ ,  $i \in [N]$ ,  $j \in [S]$ ,  $\mathbf{W} \in \{0,1\}^S$ ,  $\mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}} \in \mathbb{Z}_p^{[0..T] \times [N] \times [S] \times \{0,1\}^S}$ , define the transition coefficient as

$$\mathbf{c}_{x,w,w',\Delta i,\Delta j}(\mathbf{x};t,i,j,\mathbf{W};\mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}}) = \begin{cases} \mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}}[(t,i+\Delta i,j+\Delta j,\mathbf{W}')], & \text{if } x = \mathbf{x}[i], \ i+\Delta i \in [N], \\ w = \mathbf{W}[j], \ j+\Delta j \in [S]; \\ 0, & \text{otherwise;} \end{cases}$$

where  $\mathbf{W}' \in \{0,1\}^S$ ,  $\mathbf{W}'[j] = w'$ , and  $\mathbf{W}'[j''] = \mathbf{W}[j'']$  for all  $j'' \neq j$ .

With the above definition, Equation (8) can be restated as

<span id="page-50-1"></span>
$$\left(\mathbf{M}_{N,S}(\mathbf{x})\mathbf{r}_{t}\right)\left[(i,j,\mathbf{W},\square)\right] = \sum_{\tau \in \mathcal{T}} \mathbf{c}_{\tau}(\mathbf{x};t,i,j,\mathbf{W};\mathbf{r}_{x})\mathbf{M}_{\tau}\mathbf{r}_{f}.$$
 (9)

We are now ready to construct 1-ABE for L.

<span id="page-50-2"></span>Construction 33 (1-ABE for L). We describe the construction for any fixed value of the security parameter  $\lambda$  and suppress the appearance of  $\lambda$  below for simplicity of notations. Let the function class  $\mathcal{F}$  be

$$\mathcal{F} = \{ M|_{N,T,S} : \mathbb{Z}_p^N \to \mathbb{Z}_p \mid M \in \mathsf{TM}, N, T, S \ge 1, p \text{ prime} \}.$$

Let (Garble, Eval) be the AKGS for  $\mathcal{F}$  in Construction 30,  $\mathcal{G}$  pairing groups of order p, and (IPFE.Setup, IPFE.KeyGen, IPFE.Enc, IPFE.Dec) a secret-key IPFE based on  $\mathcal{G}$ . We construct a 1-ABE scheme based on  $\mathcal{G}$  for the following singleton predicate space  $\mathcal{P}$ :

$$X = \{(\mathbf{x}, 1^T, 1^{2^S}) \mid \mathbf{x} \in \{0, 1\}^N \text{ for some } N \ge 1, T, S \ge 1\}, \quad Y = \mathsf{TM}, P : X \times Y \to \{0, 1\}, ((\mathbf{x}, 1^T, 1^{2^S}), M) \mapsto M|_{N, T, S}(\mathbf{x}) \text{ for } \mathbf{x} \in \{0, 1\}^N, \mathcal{P} = \{P\}.$$

The 1-ABE scheme (Setup, KeyGen, Enc, Dec) operates as follows:

• Setup(P) takes the only predicate as input. It generates an IPFE master secret key  $\mathsf{msk} \xleftarrow{\$} \mathsf{IPFE}.\mathsf{Setup}(\mathfrak{s}_{\mathsf{1-ABE}})$  for the index set

$$\begin{split} \mathfrak{S}_{\text{1-ABE}} &= \left\{ \text{init, rand, rand}^{\text{comp}}, \text{rand}^{\text{temp}}, \text{rand}^{\text{temp,comp}}, \text{ acc, acc}^{\text{temp}}, \text{ sim, sim}^{\text{temp}}, \text{sim}^{\text{comp}} \right\} \\ &\quad \cup \left\{ \text{tb}_{\tau}, \text{tb}_{\tau}^{\text{comp}}, \text{tb}_{\tau}^{\text{temp}}, \text{tb}_{\tau}^{\text{temp,comp}} \ \middle| \ \tau \in \mathcal{T} \right\}. \end{split}$$

The algorithm returns msk as the master secret key.

Note: Let us explain the names of the indices: The index init is used for computing  $\ell_{\text{init}}$ . It is also used in the security proof. The indices  $\mathsf{tb}_\tau$  (short for "transition blocks") are used for computing  $\mathbf{M}_{N,S}(\mathbf{x})\mathbf{r}_t$  in  $\ell_{t,z}$ 's, rand (short for "randomizer") for  $-\mathbf{r}_{t-1}$ , and  $\mathsf{acc}$  (for "acceptance vector") for  $\alpha \mathbf{1}_{[N] \times [S] \times \{0,1\}^S} \otimes \mathbf{y}_{\mathsf{acc}}$  in  $\ell_{T+1,z}$ 's. Values at all the other indices are set to zero by the honest algorithms, and those indices are only used in the security proof. Jumping ahead, sim is used for simulating the labels, and the rest of the indices are used for holding temporary values in the hybrids; temp (resp. comp) is short for "temporary" (resp. "compensation"). More details in the proof.

• KeyGen(msk, M,  $\mu$ ) takes the master secret key, a Turing machine  $M = (Q, \mathbf{y}_{acc}, \delta) \in \mathsf{TM} = Y$ , and a pad  $\mu \in \mathbb{Z}_p$  as input. It computes the transition blocks  $\mathbf{M}_{\tau}$  for  $\tau \in \mathcal{T}$  from  $\delta$ , samples  $\mathbf{r}_f \stackrel{\$}{\sim} \mathbb{Z}_p^Q$ , and sets the vectors  $\mathbf{v}_{init}$  and  $\mathbf{v}_q$  for  $q \in [Q]$  as follows:

| vector                       | init                         | rand                          | acc                                | $tb_\tau$                                       | the other indices |
|------------------------------|------------------------------|-------------------------------|------------------------------------|-------------------------------------------------|-------------------|
| $\mathbf{v}_{\mathrm{init}}$ | $\mathbf{r}_{\mathrm{f}}[1]$ | 0                             | 0                                  | 0                                               | 0                 |
| $\mathbf{v}_q$               | 0                            | $-\mathbf{r}_{\mathrm{f}}[q]$ | $\mu \mathbf{y}_{\mathrm{acc}}[q]$ | $(\mathbf{M}_{\tau}\mathbf{r}_{\mathrm{f}})[q]$ |                   |

The algorithm generates an IPFE secret key for each vector defined above:

$$\mathsf{isk}_{\mathsf{init}} \overset{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathsf{IPFE}.\mathsf{KeyGen}(\mathsf{msk}, \llbracket \mathbf{v}_{\mathsf{init}} \rrbracket_2), \\ \mathsf{for} \ q \in [Q] \colon \ \mathsf{isk}_q \overset{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathsf{IPFE}.\mathsf{KeyGen}(\mathsf{msk}, \llbracket \mathbf{v}_q \rrbracket_2).$$

It returns  $\mathsf{sk}_M = (M, \mathsf{isk}_{\mathsf{init}}, \mathsf{isk}_1, \dots, \mathsf{isk}_Q)$  as the secret key for M encapsulating  $\mu$ .

Note: KeyGen creates the garbling (or rather, half of it) with secrets  $\alpha = \mu, \beta = 0$  so that  $\mu$  can be recovered using Eval if and only if  $M|_{N,T,S}(\mathbf{x}) \neq 0$ .

• Enc(msk,  $(\mathbf{x}, 1^T, 1^{2^S})$ ) takes the master secret key, an input string  $\mathbf{x} \in \{0, 1\}^N$  for some  $N \ge 1$ , and time/space complexity bounds  $T, S \ge 1$  (encoded as  $1^T$  and  $1^{2^S}$ ) as input. It samples  $\mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}} \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_p^{[0..T] \times [N] \times [S] \times \{0,1\}^S}$  and sets the vectors  $\mathbf{u}_{\text{init}}$  and  $\mathbf{u}_{t,i,j,\mathbf{W}}$  for  $t \in [T+1], i \in [N], j \in [S],$   $\mathbf{W} \in \{0,1\}^S$  as follows:

| vector                                           | init                                     | rand                                            | acc | $tb_{\tau}$                                                                | the other indices |
|--------------------------------------------------|------------------------------------------|-------------------------------------------------|-----|----------------------------------------------------------------------------|-------------------|
| $\mathbf{u}_{\text{init}}$                       | $ \mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}}[(0,1,1,0_S)] $ | 0                                               | 0   | 0                                                                          |                   |
| $t \leq T$ : $\mathbf{u}_{t,i,j}$ , $\mathbf{w}$ | 0                                        | $\mathbf{r}_{\mathrm{x}}[(t-1,i,j,\mathbf{W})]$ | 0   | $ \mathfrak{c}_{\tau}(\mathbf{x};t,i,j,\mathbf{W};\mathbf{r}_{\text{x}}) $ | 0                 |
| $\mathbf{u}_{T+1,i,j,\mathbf{W}}$                | 0                                        | $\mathbf{r}_{\mathrm{x}}[(T,i,j,\mathbf{W})]$   | 1   | 0                                                                          |                   |

The algorithm then generates IPFE ciphertexts for the vectors defined above:

$$\mathsf{ict}_{\mathsf{init}} \xleftarrow{\$} \mathsf{IPFE}.\mathsf{Enc}(\mathsf{msk}, \llbracket \mathbf{u}_{\mathsf{init}} \rrbracket_1),$$
 for  $t \in [T+1], i \in [N], j \in [S], \mathbf{W} \in \{0,1\}^S$ :  $\mathsf{ict}_{t,i,j,\mathbf{W}} \xleftarrow{\$} \mathsf{IPFE}.\mathsf{Enc}(\mathsf{msk}, \llbracket \mathbf{u}_{t,i,j,\mathbf{W}} \rrbracket_1).$ 

It returns  $\mathsf{ct}_{\mathbf{x},T,S} = ((\mathbf{x},T,S),\mathsf{ict}_{\mathsf{init}},(\mathsf{ict}_{t,i,j,\mathbf{W}})_{t\in[T+1],i\in[N],j\in[S],\mathbf{W}\in\{0,1\}^S})$  as the ciphertext for input  $\mathbf{x}$  with time/space bounds T,S.

• Dec(sk, ct) takes a secret key sk and a ciphertext ct as input. It parses

$$\begin{array}{ll} \mathsf{sk} \ \mathrm{as} \ \left(M, \mathsf{isk}_{\mathrm{init}}, \mathsf{isk}_1, \dots, \mathsf{isk}_Q\right) \ \mathrm{with} \ M = \left(Q, \mathbf{y}_{\mathrm{acc}}, \delta\right) \in \mathsf{TM} \qquad \mathrm{and} \\ \mathsf{ct} \ \mathrm{as} \ \left((\mathbf{x}, T, S), \mathsf{ict}_{\mathrm{init}}, (\mathsf{ict}_{t, i, j, \mathbf{W}})_{t \in [T+1], i \in [N], j \in [S], \mathbf{W} \in \{0, 1\}^S}\right) \ \mathrm{with} \ \mathbf{x} \in \{0, 1\}^N. \end{array}$$

The algorithm returns ⊥ if M|N,T,S(x) = 0. Otherwise, it computes the labels (recall that CM,N,S = [N] × [S] × {0, 1} <sup>S</sup> × [Q])

$$\llbracket \ell_{\text{init}} \rrbracket_{\text{T}} \leftarrow \mathsf{IPFE.Dec}(\mathsf{isk}_{\text{init}}, \mathsf{ict}_{\text{init}}),$$
 for  $t \in [T+1], (i, j, \mathbf{W}, q) \in \mathcal{C}_{M,N,S}$ :  $\llbracket \ell_{t,i,j,\mathbf{W},q} \rrbracket_{\text{T}} \leftarrow \mathsf{IPFE.Dec}(\mathsf{isk}_q, \mathsf{ict}_{t,i,j,\mathbf{W}}),$ 

and recovers the encapsulated pad by

$$\llbracket \mu' \rrbracket_{\mathrm{T}} \leftarrow \mathsf{Eval} \big( (M, 1^N, 1^T, 1^{2^S}, p), \mathbf{x}, \llbracket \ell_{\mathrm{init}} \rrbracket_{\mathrm{T}}, (\llbracket \ell_{t,z} \rrbracket_{\mathrm{T}})_{t \in [T+1], z \in \mathcal{C}_{M,N,S}} \big).$$

The algorithm returns [[µ 0 ]]<sup>T</sup> as the decapsulated pad.

Note: We show the correctness of the scheme, which follows by an observation that `init, (`t,z)t∈[<sup>T</sup> +1],z∈CM,N,S is a valid garbling of M|N,T,S with secrets α = µ and β = 0. Consider

$$\begin{split} &\alpha = \mu, \quad \beta = 0, \quad \mathbf{r} = \mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}} \otimes \mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{f}}, \quad \mathbf{r}_t = \mathbf{r}[(t, \mathbf{u}, \mathbf{u}, \mathbf{u}, \mathbf{u})] \ (t \in [0..T]), \\ &\left(\mathbf{L}_{\mathrm{init}}, (\mathbf{L}_{t,z})_{t \in [T+1], z \in \mathcal{C}_{M,N,S}}\right) = \mathsf{Garble}\left((M, 1^N, 1^T, 1^{2^S}, p), \alpha, \beta; \mathbf{r}\right), \end{split}$$

where the randomness used by Garble is explicitly written. Let Linit and Lt,z's be the label functions (affine in x with coefficient vectors Linit and Lt,z's, respectively). First, by the correctness of IPFE and the definition of vectors vinit and uinit, we have

$$\ell_{\text{init}} = \mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}}[(0, 1, 1, \mathbf{0}_S)]\mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{f}}[1] = \mathbf{r}_{0}[(1, 1, \mathbf{0}_S, 1)] = \beta + \mathbf{e}_{(1, 1, \mathbf{0}_S, 1)}^{\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{r}_{0} = L_{\text{init}}(\mathbf{x}).$$

Next, by the correctness of IPFE and the definition of vectors v<sup>q</sup> and ut,i,j,W, we have

$$\ell_{t,i,j,\mathbf{W},q} = -\mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}}[(t-1,i,j,\mathbf{W})]\mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{f}}[q] + \sum_{\tau \in \mathcal{T}} \mathbf{c}_{\tau}(\mathbf{x};t,i,j,\mathbf{W};\mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}})(\mathbf{M}_{\tau}\mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{f}})[q]$$

$$= -\mathbf{r}_{t-1}[(i,j,\mathbf{W},q)] + \left(\sum_{\tau \in \mathcal{T}} \mathbf{c}_{\tau}(\mathbf{x};t,i,j,\mathbf{W};\mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}})\mathbf{M}_{\tau}\mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{f}}\right)[q]$$
(Equation (9))
$$= -\mathbf{r}_{t-1}[(i,j,\mathbf{W},q)] + \left(\mathbf{M}_{N,S}(\mathbf{x})\mathbf{r}_{t}\right)[(i,j,\mathbf{W},\square)][q]$$

$$= -\mathbf{r}_{t-1}[(i,j,\mathbf{W},q)] + \left(\mathbf{M}_{N,S}(\mathbf{x})\mathbf{r}_{t}\right)[(i,j,\mathbf{W},q)]$$

$$= L_{t,i,j,\mathbf{W},q}(\mathbf{x}) \quad \text{for all } t \in [T], (i,j,\mathbf{W},q) \in \mathcal{C}_{M,N,S},$$

$$\ell_{T+1,i,j,\mathbf{W},q} = -\mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}}[(T,i,j,\mathbf{W})]\mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{f}}[q] + \alpha \mathbf{y}_{\mathrm{acc}}[q]$$

$$= -\mathbf{r}_{T}[(i,j,\mathbf{W},q)] + \alpha (\mathbf{1}_{[N]\times[S]\times\{0,1\}^{S}}\otimes\mathbf{y}_{\mathrm{acc}})[(i,j,\mathbf{W},q)]$$

$$= L_{T+1,i,j,\mathbf{W},q}(\mathbf{x}) \quad \text{for all } (i,j,\mathbf{W},q) \in \mathcal{C}_{M,N,S}.$$

Lastly, by the linearity of Eval in the labels, we can evaluate the garbling in the exponent of the target group and obtain µ <sup>0</sup> = αM|N,T,S(x) + β = µ (note that M|N,T,S(x) is either 0 or 1 for x ∈ {0, 1} <sup>N</sup> ) in the exponent. Therefore, Dec correctly decapsulates the pad.

<u>Remarks.</u> The 1-ABE scheme for L based on MDDH<sub>k</sub> can be obtained by modifying the above scheme to use pseudorandomness  $\mathbf{r} = \mathbf{R}_{\mathbf{x}}^{\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{R}_{\mathbf{f}}$  for  $\mathbf{R}_{\mathbf{x}} \overset{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_{p}^{[k] \times ([0..T] \times [N] \times [S] \times \{0,1\}^{S})}$  and  $\mathbf{R}_{\mathbf{f}} \overset{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_{p}^{k \times Q}$ .

<span id="page-53-0"></span>**Theorem 34.** Suppose in Construction 33, the SXDH assumption holds in  $\mathcal{G}$  and the IPFE scheme is function-hiding, then the constructed 1-ABE scheme is 1-key 1-ciphertext secure.

**Proof Idea.** We discuss the high-level ideas of the proof.

Recall that in the proof of adaptive security of 1-ABE for ABPs (Theorem 25), for the case where the secret key query appears before the ciphertext challenge, we gradually replace the label functions in the secret key by labels simulated as random values, except that the first label is reversely sampled.

That approach, however, fails for Construction 33 for two reasons: i) the garbling uses pseudorandomness instead of true randomness; ii) there is not enough space in the ciphertext, the secret key, or both to embed  $\Omega(TNS2^SQ)$  labels simulated as random values. We make two tweaks to the proof of Theorem 25 to solve the problems: i) we rely on the SXDH assumption to gradually switch pseudorandomness to true randomness so that by special piecewise security, we can simulate the labels as random; ii) in the final hybrid, the labels are simulated as pseudorandom values, which can be embedded in the ciphertext and the secret key.

At a high level, the proof involves 3 groups of hybrids manipulating the vectors encrypted by IPFE:

- 1. The first few hybrids replace the first label function  $L_{\text{init}}$  jointly encoded in  $\mathbf{u}_{\text{init}}$ ,  $\mathbf{v}_{\text{init}}$  by the reversely sampled first label  $\ell_{\text{init}}$  hardwired in either  $\mathbf{u}_{\text{init}}$  or  $\mathbf{v}_{\text{init}}$ , whichever is generated later.
- 2. The middle hybrids are a loop. Along the hybrids, we gradually replace the label functions  $L_{t,i,j,\mathbf{W},q}$  (jointly encoded in  $\mathbf{u}_{t,i,j,\mathbf{W}}$ 's and  $\mathbf{v}_q$ 's) generated using pseudorandomness by simulated labels  $\ell_{t,i,j,\mathbf{W},q} = \mathbf{s}_{\mathbf{x}}[(t,i,j,\mathbf{W})]\mathbf{s}_{\mathbf{f}}[q]$ , where  $\mathbf{s}_{\mathbf{x}} \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_p^{[T+1]\times[N]\times[S]\times\{0,1\}^S}$  is embedded in  $\mathbf{u}_{t,i,j,\mathbf{W}}$ 's and  $\mathbf{s}_{\mathbf{f}} \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_p^Q$  is embedded in  $\mathbf{v}_q$ 's. How the loop works depends on whether the ciphertext challenge comes first or second.
- 3. The last few hybrids do some clean-up work to completely remove  $\mu^0$  from the vectors so that it is information-theoretically hidden.

We elaborate on the loop hybrids. The reason why the strategy depends on whether the ciphertext challenge comes first or second is that we need to invoke the DDH assumption to temporarily make some label, say  $\ell_{t,i,j,\mathbf{W},q}$ , truly random. The reduction algorithm (reducing neighboring indistinguishability to DDH) needs to reversely sample  $\ell_{\text{init}}$  using RevSamp, which takes as input  $M, \mathbf{x}, T, S$  and all the other labels  $\ell_{t',i',j',\mathbf{W}',q'}$ , including  $\ell_{t,i,j,\mathbf{W},q}$ . On one hand, since  $M, \mathbf{x}, T, S$  are only fully specified after both the key and ciphertext queries are made,  $\ell_{\text{init}}$  can only be embedded in the key if it comes after the ciphertext, and in the ciphertext otherwise. On the other hand, since  $\ell_{t,i,j,\mathbf{W},q}$  is being switched from pseudorandom to random by DDH, the reduction only has access to  $\ell_{t,i,j,\mathbf{W},q}$  in the exponent of the group  $G_b$  where DDH is invoked. Thus,  $\ell_{\text{init}}$  must be reversely sampled in the exponent of  $G_b$ . Adding these requirements together necessitates that DDH must be invoked in the same group where  $\ell_{\text{init}}$  is hardcoded:

• Case 1: The ciphertext challenge appears before the secret key query. In this case,  $\ell_{\text{init}} \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \text{RevSamp}(\cdots)$  is hardwired in  $\mathbf{v}_{\text{init}}$  (in isk<sub>init</sub>, encoded in  $G_2$ ). The middle hybrids loop over  $(t, i, j, \mathbf{W})$  in lexicographical order. In each iteration, we first move everything from  $\mathbf{u}_{t,i,j}$ ,  $\mathbf{w}$  to all the

 $\mathbf{v}_q$ 's in one shot, hardwiring the honest labels  $\ell_{t,i,j,\mathbf{W},q}$  into  $\mathbf{v}_q$  for all q. Next, we invoke DDH in  $G_2$  to switch  $\mathbf{r}_t[(i,j,\mathbf{W},q)]$  from  $\mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}}[(t,i,j,\mathbf{W})]\mathbf{r}_f[q]$  to truly random for all q, which makes the labels  $\ell_{t,i,j,\mathbf{W},q}$  truly random for all q. Then, we invoke DDH in  $G_2$  again to make  $\ell_{t,i,j,\mathbf{W},q} = \mathbf{s}_{\mathbf{x}}[(t,i,j,\mathbf{W})]\mathbf{s}_f[q]$  pseudorandom for all q. Lastly, we move  $\mathbf{s}_{\mathbf{x}}[(t,i,j,\mathbf{W})]$  from all  $\mathbf{v}_q$ 's back to  $\mathbf{u}_{t,i,j,\mathbf{W}}$ .

• Case 2: The secret key query appears before the ciphertext challenge. In this case,  $\ell_{\text{init}} \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \text{RevSamp}(\cdots)$  is hardwired in  $\mathbf{u}_{\text{init}}$  (in ict<sub>init</sub>, encoded in  $G_1$ ). The middle hybrids form a two-level loop with outer loop over t in increasing order and inner loop over q in increasing order. In each iteration, we first move all occurrences of  $\mathbf{r}_f[q]$  and  $\mathbf{s}_f[q]$  into all the  $\mathbf{u}_{t',i',j',\mathbf{W}'}$ 's in one shot (using the extra indices) and hardwire the honest labels  $\ell_{t,i,j,\mathbf{W},q}$  into  $\mathbf{u}_{t,i,j,\mathbf{W}}$ 's for all  $i, j, \mathbf{W}$ . Next, we invoke DDH in  $G_1$  to switch  $\mathbf{r}_t[(i, j, \mathbf{W}, q)]$  from  $\mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}}[(t, i, j, \mathbf{W})]\mathbf{r}_f[q]$  to truly random for all  $i, j, \mathbf{W}$ , making the labels  $\ell_{t,i,j,\mathbf{W},q}$  truly random for all  $i, j, \mathbf{W}$ . Then, we invoke DDH in  $G_1$  again to make  $\ell_{t,i,j,\mathbf{W},q} = \mathbf{s}_{\mathbf{x}}[(t,i,j,\mathbf{W})]\mathbf{s}_f[q]$  pseudorandom for all  $i, j, \mathbf{W}$ . Lastly, we move  $\mathbf{r}_f[q]$  and  $\mathbf{s}_f[q]$  back from all the  $\mathbf{u}_{t',i',j',\mathbf{W}'}$ 's.

The values must be carefully embedded in appropriate places, subject to the compactness requirement and the constraint that labels are still correctly computed, so that all the invocations of DDH are indeed valid.

We start with the first/last few hybrids, for which the two cases can be handled together, and then complete the proof by connecting the hybrids in two separate claims for the two cases.

<u>Proof (Theorem 34).</u> Let  $\mathcal{A}$  be any efficient adversary. We want to show that the distinguishing advantage of  $\mathcal{A}$  against  $\mathsf{Exp}^0_{1-\mathsf{sk},1-\mathsf{ct}}$  and  $\mathsf{Exp}^1_{1-\mathsf{sk},1-\mathsf{ct}}$  is negligible. In these two experiments, the adversary receives a single secret key  $\mathsf{sk}$  encoding  $M = (Q, \mathbf{y}_{\mathsf{acc}}, \delta)$  and secret  $\mu^0$ , and a ciphertext  $\mathsf{ct}$  encoding  $(\mathbf{x}, 1^T, 1^{2^S})$ . The only difference between these two experiments is that the adversary additionally receives either  $\mu^0$  or  $\mu^1$  and wants to distinguish them. Recall that by construction of our 1-ABE, the ciphertext  $\mathsf{ct}$  contains a set of IPFE ciphertexts ict<sub>init</sub> and ict<sub>t,i,j,\mathbf{W}</sub>'s encrypting  $\mathbf{u}_{\text{init}}$  and  $\mathbf{u}_{t,i,j,\mathbf{W}}$ 's, and  $\mathsf{sk}$  contains IPFE secret keys isk<sub>init</sub> and isk<sub>q</sub>'s encrypting  $\mathbf{v}_{\text{init}}$  and  $\mathbf{v}_q$ 's, respectively.

The first/last few hybrids are illustrated in Figure 6. The indices with superscripts are suppressed as they are only used in the loop hybrids. Note that though  $\mathbf{v}$ 's (in isk's) are listed before  $\mathbf{u}$ 's (in ict's), the argument about these hybrids is unaffected by whether the ciphertext challenge comes first or second.

- <u>Hybrid H</u><sup>b</sup><sub>0</sub> proceeds identically to  $\mathsf{Exp}^b_{\mathsf{1-sk},\mathsf{1-ct}}$ , where **v**'s contain  $\mu^0$ , **r**<sub>f</sub> and the transition blocks, and **u**'s contain **x** and **r**<sub>x</sub>.
- <u>Hybrid H</u><sup>b</sup><sub>1</sub> proceeds identically to H<sup>b</sup><sub>0</sub>, except that  $\ell_{\text{init}}$  is hardwired in  $\mathbf{u}_{\text{init}}$  or  $\mathbf{v}_{\text{init}}$ , whichever is generated later, and that  $\mathbf{s}_{\text{f}} \overset{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_p^Q$  is embedded in  $\mathbf{v}_q[\text{sim}]$ 's. More specifically, the first change is implemented as follows:
  - If the *ciphertext* challenge comes first,  $\mathbf{u}_{init}[init]$  is set to 1 (at encryption time) and  $\mathbf{v}_{init}[init]$  is set to  $\mathbf{r}_{x}[(0,1,1,\mathbf{0}_{S})]\mathbf{r}_{f}[1]$  (at key generation time).
  - If the secret key query comes first,  $\mathbf{v}_{init}[init]$  is set to 1 (at key generation time) and  $\mathbf{u}_{init}[init]$  is set to  $\mathbf{r}_{x}[(0,1,1,\mathbf{0}_{S})]\mathbf{r}_{f}[1]$  (at encryption time).

The first change prepares  $\ell_{\text{init}}$  to be reversely sampled starting in the next hybrid by hard-wiring it. The second change prepares the  $\ell_{t,i,j,\mathbf{W},q}$ 's to be simulated as pseudorandom values
