in the loop hybrids — it has no effect at this moment since the newly embedded values in  $\mathbf{v}$ 's multiply with 0 in  $\mathbf{u}$ 's. The inner products in  $\mathsf{H}_0^b$  and  $\mathsf{H}_1^b$  remain unchanged, therefore, by the function-hiding property of IPFE,  $\mathsf{H}_0^b$  and  $\mathsf{H}_1^b$  are indistinguishable.

- <u>Hybrid H</u><sup>b</sup><sub>2</sub> proceeds identically to H<sub>1</sub><sup>b</sup>, except that  $\ell_{\text{init}}$  (was  $\mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}}[(0,1,1,\mathbf{0}_S)]\mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{f}}[1]$ ) in  $\mathbf{u}_{\text{init}}$  or  $\mathbf{v}_{\text{init}}$  is reversely sampled from the other labels. By the special piecewise security of AKGS, H<sub>1</sub><sup>b</sup> and H<sub>2</sub><sup>b</sup> are identical.
- <u>Hybrid H</u><sup>b</sup><sub>4</sub> proceeds identically to H<sup>b</sup><sub>2</sub>, except that the inner products between  $\mathbf{u}_{t,i,j,\mathbf{W}}$ 's and  $\mathbf{v}_q$ 's change from the honest labels to simulated labels  $\mathbf{s}_{\mathbf{x}}[(t,i,j,\mathbf{W})]\mathbf{s}_{\mathbf{f}}[q]$ . In Figure 6, this is reflected by the  $\mathbf{u}_{t,i,j,\mathbf{W}}$ 's having their values at rand, acc and  $\mathbf{tb}_{\tau}$ 's cleared and embedding  $\mathbf{s}_{\mathbf{x}} \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_p^{[T+1]\times[N]\times[S]\times\{0,1\}^S}$  at sim. We will show  $\mathsf{H}_2^b \approx \mathsf{H}_4^b$  as two separate claims.

<span id="page-56-0"></span>Claim 35.  $H_2^b \approx H_4^b$  conditioned on Case 1.

<span id="page-56-2"></span>Claim 36.  $H_2^b \approx H_4^b$  conditioned on Case 2.

• <u>Hybrid  $H_5^b$ </u> proceeds identically to  $H_4^b$ , except that all the  $\mathbf{v}_q$ 's have their (leftover) values at rand, acc and  $\mathbf{tb}_{\tau}$ 's cleared. These values multiply with 0 in  $\mathbf{u}$ 's in  $H_4^b$ , so the inner products remain unchanged, and  $H_5^b \approx H_4^b$  by the function-hiding property of IPFE.

Observe that  $\mathsf{H}^0_5 \equiv \mathsf{H}^1_5$  — since  $\mu^0$  never appears in the vectors, both  $\mu^0$  and  $\mu^1$  are just uniformly random values independent of everything else in the hybrids. By a hybrid argument, we conclude  $\mathsf{Exp}^0_{1\text{-sk},1\text{-ct}} \approx \mathsf{Exp}^1_{1\text{-sk},1\text{-ct}}$ .

<u>Proof (Claim 35).</u> For Case 1, we show  $\mathsf{H}_2^b \approx \mathsf{H}_4^b$  via a series of hybrids  $\mathsf{H}_{3,t,i,j,\mathbf{W},1},\ldots,\mathsf{H}_{3,t,i,j,\mathbf{W},5}^b$  for  $(t,i,j,\mathbf{W}) \in [T+1] \times [N] \times [S] \times \{0,1\}^S$  in lexicographical order. Denote by  $(t,i,j,\mathbf{W})+1$  the next tuple of indices in increasing order.

The hybrids are illustrated in Figure 7. Note that the  $\mathbf{u}$ 's are listed before the  $\mathbf{v}$ 's, as in Case 1, the ciphertext is generated before the secret key. In the figure, all the indices with superscripts except  $\mathsf{sim}^\mathsf{temp}$  (temp means "temporary") are suppressed as they are not used. 15

- <u>Hybrid H</u><sup>b</sup><sub>3,t,i,j,**W**,1</sub> proceeds identically to H<sup>b</sup><sub>2</sub>, except that for all  $(t',i',j',\mathbf{W}') < (t,i,j,\mathbf{W})$ ,  $\mathbf{u}_{t',i',j',\mathbf{W}'}$  has its values in rand, acc and  $\mathbf{tb}_{\tau}$ 's cleared, and that a random value  $\mathbf{s}_{\mathbf{x}}[t',i',j',\mathbf{W}']$  is embedded in  $\mathbf{u}_{t',i',j',\mathbf{W}'}[\mathbf{sim}]$ . This means all the labels with  $(t',i',j',\mathbf{W}') < (t,i,j,\mathbf{W})$  are simulated, the first label  $\ell_{\text{init}}$  is reversely sampled, and the rest are honestly computed.
- <u>Hybrid  $H_{3,t,i,j,\mathbf{W},2}^b$ </u> proceeds identically to  $H_{3,t,i,j,\mathbf{W},1}^b$ , except that the values in  $\mathbf{u}_{t,i,j,\mathbf{W}}$  are zeroed out, and its inner products with all  $\mathbf{v}_q$ 's the labels  $\ell_{t,i,j,\mathbf{W},q}$  for all q's are hardcoded into  $\mathbf{v}_q$ 's:
  - The values of  $\mathbf{u}_{t,i,j,\mathbf{W}}$  at rand, acc and  $\mathsf{tb}_{\tau}$ 's are set to 0.
  - $-\mathbf{u}_{t,i,j,\mathbf{W}}[\mathsf{sim}^\mathsf{temp}]$  is set to 1 to pick up the values  $\mathbf{v}_q[\mathsf{sim}^\mathsf{temp}]$  for all q.
  - The honest labels  $\ell_{t,i,j,\mathbf{W},q} = -\mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}}[(t-1,i,j,\mathbf{W})]\mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{f}}[q] + \cdots$  are embedded in  $\mathbf{v}_{q}[\mathsf{sim}^{\mathsf{temp}}]$  for each  $q \in [Q]$ , where "···" is either  $\mu^{0}\mathbf{y}_{\mathrm{acc}}[q]$  (if t = T+1) or  $\sum_{\tau \in \mathcal{T}} \mathbf{c}_{\tau}(\mathbf{x};t,i,j,\mathbf{W};\mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}})(\mathbf{M}_{\tau}\mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{f}})[q]$  (if  $t \leq T$ ; it is  $(\mathbf{M}_{N,S}\mathbf{r}_{t})[(t,i,j,\mathbf{W},q)]$  for pseudorandom  $\mathbf{r}_{t} = \mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}}[t, \mathbf{u}, \mathbf{u}, \mathbf{u}, \mathbf{u}] \otimes \mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{f}}$ ).

<span id="page-56-1"></span> $<sup>^{15}</sup>$ Case 1 is the simpler case, though it is already not simple. Note that this coincides with the selective (or semi-adaptive) case, but the simplicity is more of a consequence of the AKGS structure than that of selectivity.

For brevity,  $\mathbf{u}_{\text{init}}$  and  $\mathbf{v}_{\text{init}}$  are suppressed. The reversely sampled  $\ell_{\text{init}}$  is hardwired in  $\mathbf{v}_{\text{init}}$ , and is only needed (and can only be computed so by the reduction) in the exponent of  $G_2$ :

$$[\![\ell_{\mathrm{init}}]\!]_2 \leftarrow \mathsf{RevSamp}\big((M, 1^N, 1^T, 1^{2^S}), \mathbf{x}, [\![0]\!]_2, ([\![\ell_{t,z}]\!]_2)_{t \in [T+1], z \in \mathcal{C}_{M,N,S}}\big).$$

In the intermediate hybrids,  $\mathbf{u}_{t',i',j',\mathbf{W}'}$ 's are suppressed. They remain unchanged in this iteration. The choices between "0 or 1" and " $\mathbf{c}_{\tau}(\cdots)$  or 0" are the former if  $t' \leq T$ , and the latter if t' = T + 1.

In this interation, the labels  $\ell_{t',i',j',\mathbf{W}',q}$  with  $(t',i',j',\mathbf{W}')$ ... are...

 $<(t,i,j,\mathbf{W})$ : simulated as  $\mathbf{s}_{\mathbf{x}}[(t',i',j',\mathbf{W}')]\mathbf{s}_{\mathbf{f}}[q]$  and computed using IPFE

 $=(t,i,j,\mathbf{W})$ : computed honestly using IPFE

→ computed honestly and hardwired in sk

 $\rightarrow$  simulated as random and hardwired in  $\mathsf{sk}$ 

 $\rightarrow$  simulated as  $\mathbf{s}_{\mathbf{x}}[(t,i,j,\mathbf{W})]\mathbf{s}_{\mathbf{f}}[q]$  and hardwired in  $\mathsf{sk}$ 

 $\rightarrow$  simulated as  $\mathbf{s}_{\mathbf{x}}[(t,i,j,\mathbf{W})]\mathbf{s}_{\mathbf{f}}[q]$  and computed using IPFE

 $> (t, i, j, \mathbf{W})$ : computed honestly using IPFE

When a label is computed honestly, the garbling randomness is  $\mathbf{r} = \mathbf{r}_x \otimes \mathbf{r}_f$ .

When a label is computed using IPFE,  $\mathbf{r}_x, \mathbf{s}_x$  components are in  $\mathsf{ct}$  and  $\mathbf{r}_f, \mathbf{s}_f$  components are in  $\mathsf{sk}$ .

Figure 7: The loop hybrids in the security proof of 1-ABE for L for the case where the ciphertext challenge comes before the secret key query.

As depicted in Figure 7, the inner products in  $\mathsf{H}^b_{3,t,i,j,\mathbf{W},1}$  and  $\mathsf{H}^b_{3,t,i,j,\mathbf{W},2}$  remain unchanged, so they are indistinguishable by the function-hiding property of IPFE.

• <u>Hybrid  $H_{3,t,i,j,\mathbf{W},3}^b$ </u> proceeds identically to  $H_{3,t,i,j,\mathbf{W},2}^b$ , except that the labels  $\ell_{t,i,j,\mathbf{W},q}$  are replaced by truly random values. Observe that in both  $H_{3,t,i,j,\mathbf{W},2}^b$  and  $H_{3,t,i,j,\mathbf{W},3}^b$ , the random values  $\mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}}[(t-1,i,j,\mathbf{W})]$  and  $\mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{f}}[q]$ 's only appear in  $G_2$  (the group encoding secret key vectors). The indistinguishability between them reduces to the DDH assumption in  $G_2$ : Given an MDDH<sub>1,q</sub> challenge

$$\begin{aligned} & & & & & & & & & & & & & & & & & & &$$

we compute the labels  $\ell_{t,i,j,\mathbf{W},q}$  as  $-z_q + \cdots$ . If a DDH tuple is given, these labels use pseudorandom randomizers  $\mathbf{r}_{t-1}[(i,j,\mathbf{W}, \omega)] = \mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}}[(t-1,i,j,\mathbf{W})]\mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{f}}$  as in  $\mathsf{H}^b_{3,t,i,j,\mathbf{W},2}$ . If a truly random tuple is given, these labels use truly random randomizers  $\mathbf{r}_{t-1}[(i,j,\mathbf{W},\omega)] \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_p^Q$ , thus are themselves truly random (as in  $\mathsf{H}^b_{3,t,i,j,\mathbf{W},3}$ ) due to the special piecewise security of AKGS. Note that everything else in the two hybrids can be efficiently computed — in particular, the value  $[\![\ell_{\mathrm{init}}]\!]_2 \leftarrow \mathsf{RevSamp}(\cdots)$  can be computed efficiently in the exponent.

- <u>Hybrid H</u><sup>b</sup><sub>3,t,i,j,**W**,4</sub> proceeds identically to H<sup>b</sup><sub>3,t,i,j,**W**,3</sub>, except that the truly random labels  $\ell_{t,i,j,\mathbf{W},q}$  for all  $q \in [Q]$  are replaced by pseudorandom values  $\mathbf{s}_{\mathbf{x}}[(t,i,j,\mathbf{W})]\mathbf{s}_{\mathbf{f}}[q]$  with  $\mathbf{s}_{\mathbf{x}}[(t,i,j,\mathbf{W})] \overset{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_p$ . The indistinguishability between the two hybrids reduces to the DDH assumption in  $G_2$ .
- <u>Hybrid H</u><sup>b</sup><sub>3,t,i,j,**W**,5</sub> proceeds identically to H<sup>b</sup><sub>3,t,i,j,**W**,4</sub>, except that the pseudorandom labels  $\ell_{t,i,j,\mathbf{W},q} = \mathbf{s}_{\mathbf{x}}[(t,i,j,\mathbf{W})]\mathbf{s}_{\mathbf{f}}[q]$  hardwired in  $\mathbf{v}_{q}[\mathsf{sim}^{\mathsf{temp}}]$ 's are *split* into  $\mathbf{u}_{t,i,j,\mathbf{W}}[\mathsf{sim}]$  (embedding the factor  $\mathbf{s}_{\mathbf{x}}[(t,i,j,\mathbf{W})]$ ) and  $\mathbf{v}_{q}[\mathsf{sim}]$ 's (embedding the factor  $\mathbf{s}_{\mathbf{f}}[q]$ ), as shown in Figure 7. The inner products in H<sup>b</sup><sub>3,t,i,j,**W**,4</sub> and H<sup>b</sup><sub>3,t,i,j,**W**,5</sub> remain unchanged, so the two hybrids are indistinguishable by the function-hiding property of IPFE. Moreover, H<sup>b</sup><sub>3,t,i,j,**W**,5</sub>  $\equiv$  H<sup>b</sup><sub>3,t',i',j',**W**',1</sub> for  $(t',i',j',\mathbf{W}') = (t,i,j,\mathbf{W}) + 1$ .

By a hybrid argument, we have  $\mathsf{H}^b_{3,1,1,1,\mathbf{0}_S,1} \approx \mathsf{H}^b_{3,T+1,N,S,\mathbf{1}_S,5}$ . Lastly, observe that  $\mathsf{H}^b_{3,1,1,1,\mathbf{0}_S,1} \equiv \mathsf{H}^b_2$  and  $\mathsf{H}^b_{3,T+1,N,S,\mathbf{1}_S,5} \equiv \mathsf{H}^b_4$ . Therefore,  $\mathsf{H}^b_2 \approx \mathsf{H}^b_4$  conditioned on Case 1.

<u>Proof (Claim 36)</u>. The proof of  $\mathsf{H}_2^b \approx \mathsf{H}_4^b$  is more involved in Case 2. In this case, the ciphertext challenge appears after the secret key query, and we must hardwire the reversely sampled  $\ell_{\text{init}}$  in the ciphertext.

Suppose at some point, we want to make  $\ell_{t,i,j,\mathbf{W},q}$  truly random by invoking DDH. In Case 1, we move  $\mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}}[(t-1,i,j,\mathbf{W})]$  into the secret key vectors, which is easy because by the time we need to invoke DDH on  $\mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}}[(t-1,i,j,\mathbf{W})]$ , it only appears in one place (namely, in  $\mathbf{u}_{t,i,j,\mathbf{W}}[\mathsf{rand}]$ ) and goes away after the invocation of DDH. In Case 2, since  $\ell_{\text{init}} \leftarrow \mathsf{RevSamp}(\cdots)$  must be computed in the exponent in  $G_1$ , the only option is to move  $\mathbf{r}_f[q]$  into the ciphertext vectors. However, depending on the transition blocks,  $\mathbf{r}_f[q]$  might appear in  $(\mathbf{M}_\tau \mathbf{r}_f)[q']$  of any  $\mathbf{v}_{q'}$ . There are many limitations to take into consideration when sorting out the proof:

<span id="page-58-0"></span><sup>&</sup>lt;sup>16</sup>Note that this is the first hybrid in which  $\mathbf{s}_{\mathbf{x}}[(t,i,j,\mathbf{W})]$  appears — each such value is introduced only when needed.

- The special piecewise security only allows us to simulate  $\ell_{t,i,j,\mathbf{W},q}$ 's in increasing order of t.
- To simulate  $\ell_{t,i,j,\mathbf{W},q}$ , all occurrences of  $\mathbf{r}_{\mathrm{f}}[q]$  must be in the ciphertext.
- There is not enough space in the ciphertext to embed all the  $\mathbf{r}_{\mathrm{f}}[q]$ 's at the same time.
- The value  $\mathbf{r}_{\mathrm{f}}[q]$  must *not* go away until *all*  $\ell_{t,i,j,\mathbf{W},q}$ 's are simulated. Indeed,  $\mathbf{r}_{\mathrm{f}}[q]$  still resides in  $\mathbf{v}_{q'}$ 's in  $\mathsf{H}_4^b$ , the end hybrid (for this claim).

Combining these factors, a feasible strategy is to switch (in increasing order of t, q) batches of  $NS2^S$  label functions (i.e., for fixed t, q and all  $i, j, \mathbf{W}$ ) into simulated labels by moving  $\mathbf{r}_f[q]$ 's back and forth in each iteration (to keep the labels correctly computed) until all the labels are simulated. The above also applies to  $\mathbf{s}_f[q]$  when we consider invoking DDH again to make truly random labels only pseudorandom.

More specifically, in iteration t, q, when moving  $\mathbf{r}_{\mathrm{f}}[q]$  into the ciphertext vectors, we erase all its occurrences in the secret key vectors and must *compensate* some  $\ell_{t',i,j,\mathbf{W},q'}$ 's for their loss of  $\mathbf{r}_{\mathrm{f}}[q]$  using the indices with superscript **comp**. This is done by separating out the terms with  $\mathbf{r}_{\mathrm{f}}[q]$ . See the compensation identity in the notes of Figure 9 for details.

<span id="page-59-0"></span>To better understand the procedure, we define the modes of a label  $\ell_{t',i,j,\mathbf{W},q'}$ . There are three orthogonal groups of modes. Each label has one mode in each group. We will refer to these modes in the description of hybrids below, their meaning will also become clearer in the context of hybrids.

- The first group is about the value of the label. A label is *honest* if its value is  $L_{t',i,j,\mathbf{W},q'}(\mathbf{x})$  with garbling randomness set to  $\mathbf{r} = \mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}} \otimes \mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{f}}$ . It is *random* if its value is sampled uniformly at random. It is *simulated* if its value is  $\mathbf{s}_{\mathbf{x}}[(t',i,j,\mathbf{W})]\mathbf{s}_{\mathbf{f}}[q']$ .
- The second group is about where the terms  $\mathbf{r}_f$ ,  $\mathbf{s}_f$  of a label resides. A label is normal (this is the default) if  $\mathbf{r}_f$ ,  $\mathbf{s}_f$  resides in the secret key. It is *compensated* if  $\mathbf{r}_f[q]$ ,  $\mathbf{s}_f[q]$  are in the ciphertext with the other components of  $\mathbf{r}_f$ ,  $\mathbf{s}_f$  in the secret key. It is *hardwired* if the value (in its entirety) is hardwired in the ciphertext (for conceptual simplicity, this mode only applies to the labels with t' = t, q' = q). A non-normal label will use indices with superscript comp.
- The last group is a highly technical one. A label is normal (default) if it is computed without indices with superscript temp. It is *temporary* if it is computed with indices with superscript temp (a label can be in this mode only when t' = t).

The loop hybrids are a *two-level loop* with outer loop over t = 1, ..., T + 1 (Figure 8) and inner loop over q = 1, ..., Q (Figure 9). In these hybrids, **u**'s (in ict's) appear after **v**'s (in isk's). The outer loop consists of the following hybrids:

- <u>Hybrid H</u><sup>b</sup><sub>3,t,1</sub> proceeds identically to H<sup>b</sup><sub>2</sub>, except that for all t' < t and all  $i, j, \mathbf{W}$ , the vectors  $\mathbf{u}_{t',i,j,\mathbf{W}}$  have their values at rand, acc and  $\mathsf{tb}_{\tau}$ 's cleared and embed  $\mathbf{s}_{\mathbf{x}}[(t',i,j,\mathbf{W})]$  at sim. In this hybrid, labels with t = t' are in the *honest* mode.
- <u>Hybrid H</u><sup>b</sup><sub>3,t,2</sub> proceeds identically to H<sup>b</sup><sub>3,t,1</sub>, except that the mode of  $\ell_{t,i,j,\mathbf{W},q}$ 's (for all  $i, j, \mathbf{W}, q$ ) are changed to *honest and temporary*, and that a random value  $\mathbf{s}_{\mathbf{x}}[(t,i,j,\mathbf{W})]$  is embedded in  $\mathbf{u}_{t,i,j,\mathbf{W}}[\mathsf{sim}^{\mathsf{temp}}]$  for all  $i, j, \mathbf{W}$ . The first change is implemented as follows:
  - For all q, the values of  $\mathbf{v}_q$ 's at rand, acc and  $\mathsf{tb}_\tau$  are *copied* to their counterparts with superscript temp.

<span id="page-60-0"></span>

For brevity,  $\mathbf{u}_{\mathrm{init}}$  and  $\mathbf{v}_{\mathrm{init}}$  are suppressed.

The reversely sampled  $\ell_{\rm init}$  is hardwired in  $\mathbf{u}_{\rm init}$ :

$$\ell_{\text{init}} \leftarrow \mathsf{RevSamp}\big((M, 1^N, 1^T, 1^{2^S}), \mathbf{x}, 0, (\ell_{t,z})_{t \in [T+1], z \in \mathcal{C}_{M,N,S}}\big).$$

The "normal" in... rand, rand temp acc, acc temp 
$$\mathbf{t}b_{\tau}$$
,  $\mathbf{t}b_{\tau}^{\text{temp}}$ 

$$\mathbf{v}_{q} : -\mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{f}}[q] \qquad \mu^{0}\mathbf{y}_{\text{acc}}[q] \qquad (\mathbf{M}_{\tau}\mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{f}})[q]$$

$$t' \leq T, \mathbf{u}_{t',i,j,\mathbf{W}} : \mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}}[t'-1,i,j,\mathbf{W}] \qquad 0 \qquad \mathfrak{c}(\mathbf{x};t',i,j,\mathbf{W})$$

$$\mathbf{u}_{T+1,i,j,\mathbf{W}} : \mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}}[T,i,j,\mathbf{W}] \qquad 1 \qquad 0$$

In this iteration, the *modes* of  $\ell_{t',i,j,\mathbf{W},q}$  are...

t' < t: simulated

t'=t: honest  $\to$  honest and temporary  $\to$  simulated and temporary  $\to$  simulated

t' > t: honest

Figure 8: The outer loop hybrids in the security proof of 1-ABE for L for the case where the ciphertext challenge comes after the secret key query.

- For all  $i, j, \mathbf{W}$ , the values of  $\mathbf{u}_{t,i,j,\mathbf{W}}$ 's at rand, acc and  $\mathsf{tb}_{\tau}$  are *moved* to their counterparts with superscript temp.

This way, the labels are still correctly computed, i.e., the inner products remain unchanged. The second change prepares  $\ell_{t,i,j,\mathbf{W},q}$ 's to be simulated and currently has no effect — the newly embedded values multiply with 0 in the  $\mathbf{v}_q$ 's. Since the inner products remain unchanged,  $\mathsf{H}^b_{3,t,1} \approx \mathsf{H}^b_{3,t,2}$  by the function-hiding property of IPFE.

- <u>Hybrid H</u><sup>b</sup><sub>3,t,4</sub> proceeds identically to H<sup>b</sup><sub>3,t,2</sub>, except that the mode of  $\ell_{t,i,j,\mathbf{W},q}$ 's (for all  $i,j,\mathbf{W},q$ ) is switched from honest and temporary to simulated and temporary. In Figure 8, this is reflected by  $\mathbf{v}_q$ 's (for all q) having their values at rand<sup>temp</sup>, acc<sup>temp</sup> and  $\mathbf{tb}_{\tau}^{\text{temp}}$ 's cleared and embedding  $\mathbf{s}_f[q]$  at sim<sup>temp</sup>. We will show  $\mathsf{H}_{3,t,2}^b \approx \mathsf{H}_{3,t,4}^b$  via a subseries of hybrids (the inner loop hybrids).
- <u>Hybrid  $H_{3,t,5}^b$ </u> proceeds identically to  $H_{3,t,4}^b$ , except that the mode of  $\ell_{t,i,j,\mathbf{W},q}$ 's is switched from *simulated and temporary* to *simulated* and some clean-up work is done in preparation for the next iteration:
  - $-\mathbf{v}_{q}$ 's (for all q) have their values at sim<sup>temp</sup> cleared.
  - $-\mathbf{u}_{t,i,j,\mathbf{W}}$ 's (for all  $i,j,\mathbf{W}$ ) have  $\mathbf{s}_{\mathrm{f}}[(t,i,j,\mathbf{W})]$ 's moved from  $\mathsf{sim}^{\mathsf{temp}}$  into  $\mathsf{sim}$ .
  - $-\mathbf{u}_{t,i,j,\mathbf{W}}$ 's (for all  $i, j, \mathbf{W}$ ) have their values at rand<sup>temp</sup>, acc<sup>temp</sup> and  $\mathbf{tb}_{\tau}^{\mathsf{temp}}$ 's cleared.

It is easy to check that the inner products remain unchanged, so  $\mathsf{H}^b_{3,t,4} \approx \mathsf{H}^b_{3,t,5}$  by the function-hiding property of IPFE. Furthermore, we have  $\mathsf{H}^b_{3,t,5} \equiv \mathsf{H}^b_{3,t+1,1}$ .

Observe that  $\mathsf{H}^b_{3,1,1} \equiv \mathsf{H}^b_2$  and  $\mathsf{H}^b_{3,T+2,5} \equiv \mathsf{H}^b_4$ . Once we prove  $\mathsf{H}^b_{3,t,2} \approx \mathsf{H}^b_{3,t,4}$ , we can conclude  $\mathsf{H}^b_2 \approx \mathsf{H}^b_4$  by a hybrid argument.

The inner loop hybrids connect  $\mathsf{H}^b_{3,t,2}$  and  $\mathsf{H}^b_{3,t,4}$  by switching  $\ell_{t,i,j,\mathbf{W},q}$  from honest and temporary to simulated and temporary one by one for  $q=1,\ldots,Q$ :

- <u>Hybrid H</u><sup>b</sup><sub>3,t,3,q,1</sub> proceeds identically to H<sup>b</sup><sub>3,t,2</sub>, except that for q' < q, all the  $\mathbf{v}_{q'}$  have their values at rand<sup>temp</sup>, acc<sup>temp</sup> and tb<sup>temp</sup>; s cleared, and the value  $\mathbf{s}_{\mathbf{f}}[q']$  is embedded at sim<sup>temp</sup>, i.e., the labels  $\ell_{t,i,j,\mathbf{W},q'}$  for all  $i,j,\mathbf{W}$  and all q' < q have been switched from honest and temporary to simulated and temporary.
- <u>Hybrid H</u><sup>b</sup><sub>3,t,3,q,2</sub> proceeds identically to H<sup>b</sup><sub>3,t,3,q,1</sub>, except that all occurrences of  $\mathbf{r}_{\mathrm{f}}[q]$  and  $\mathbf{s}_{\mathrm{f}}[q]$  are moved from  $\mathbf{v}_{q'}$ 's into  $\mathbf{v}_{t',i,j,\mathbf{W}}$ 's according to the compensation identity. The implementation is illustrated in Figure 9. The labels with q'=q or t'>t or t'=t, q'>q gain compensated mode on top of their existing modes, and the labels  $\ell_{t,i,j,\mathbf{W},q}$  for all  $i,j,\mathbf{W}$  become honest and hardwired (hardwired in  $\mathbf{u}_{t,i,j,\mathbf{W}}[\mathsf{sim}^{\mathsf{comp}}]$ ). The inner products (the labels) remain unchanged, so  $\mathsf{H}^b_{3,t,3,q,1} \approx \mathsf{H}^b_{3,t,3,q,2}$  by the function-hiding property of IPFE.
- <u>Hybrid</u>  $H_{3,t,3,q,3}^b$  proceeds identically to  $H_{3,t,3,q,2}^b$ , except the labels  $\ell_{t,i,j,\mathbf{W},q}$  (for all  $i, j, \mathbf{W}$ ) hardwired in  $\mathbf{u}_{t,i,j,\mathbf{W}}[\mathsf{sim}^\mathsf{comp}]$  become random and hardwired. The indistinguishability between  $H_{3,t,3,q,2}^b$  and  $H_{3,t,3,q,3}^b$  reduces to the DDH assumption in  $G_1$ .
- <u>Hybrid H</u><sup>b</sup><sub>3,t,3,q,4</sub> proceeds identically to H<sup>b</sup><sub>3,t,3,q,2</sub>, except the labels  $\ell_{t,i,j,\mathbf{W},q}$  (for all  $i,j,\mathbf{W}$ ) hardwired in  $\mathbf{u}_{t,i,j,\mathbf{W}}[\mathsf{sim}^{\mathsf{comp}}]$  are changed to be pseudorandom  $\mathbf{s}_{\mathbf{x}}[(t,i,j,\mathbf{W})]\mathbf{s}_{\mathbf{f}}[q]$ , which makes them *simulated and hardwired*. The indistinguishability between H<sup>b</sup><sub>3,t,3,q,2</sub> and H<sup>b</sup><sub>3,t,3,q,3</sub> again reduces to the DDH assumption in  $G_1$ .

Figure 9: The inner loop hybrids in the security proof of 1-ABE for L for the case where the ciphertext challenge comes after the secret key query (notes).

<span id="page-63-1"></span>For brevity,  $\mathbf{u}_{\text{init}}$  and  $\mathbf{v}_{\text{init}}$  are suppressed. The reversely sampled  $\ell_{\text{init}}$  is hardwired in  $\mathbf{u}_{\text{init}}$ , and is only needed (and can only be computed so by the reduction) in the exponent of  $G_1$ :

$$[\![\ell_{\mathrm{init}}]\!]_1 \leftarrow \mathsf{RevSamp} \big( (M, 1^N, 1^T, 1^{2^S}), \mathbf{x}, [\![0]\!]_1, ([\![\ell_{t,z}]\!]_1)_{t \in [T+1], z \in \mathcal{C}_{M,N,S}} \big).$$

$$\begin{array}{cccccccccccccccccccccccccccccccccccc$$

The compensation ( $\mathbf{x} \ \mathbf{r}_{\mathrm{f}}[q], \mathbf{1} \ \mathbf{r}_{\mathrm{f}}[q]$ ) components in...

$$\begin{aligned} & & & & & & & & & & & & & & & & & & &$$

 $\mathbf{u}_{T+1,i,j,\mathbf{W}} \cdot \mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}[(T,i,j,\mathbf{W})]} \cdot \mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}[(T,i,j,\mathbf{W})]} \mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}[(T,i,j,\mathbf{W})]} \mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}[(T,i,j,\mathbf{W})]} \mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}[(T,i,j,\mathbf{W})]} \mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}[(T,i,j,\mathbf{W})]} \mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}[(T,i,j,\mathbf{W})]} \mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}[(T,i,j,\mathbf{W})]} \mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}[(T,i,j,\mathbf{W})]} \mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}[(T,i,j,\mathbf{W})]} \mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}[(T,i,j,\mathbf{W})]} \mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}[(T,i,j,\mathbf{W})]} \mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}[(T,i,j,\mathbf{W})]} \mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}[(T,i,j,\mathbf{W})]} \mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}[(T,i,j,\mathbf{W})]} \mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}[(T,i,j,\mathbf{W})]} \mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}[(T,i,j,\mathbf{W})]} \mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}[(T,i,j,\mathbf{W})]} \mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}[(T,i,j,\mathbf{W})]} \mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}[(T,i,j,\mathbf{W})]} \mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}[(T,i,j,\mathbf{W})]} \mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}[(T,i,j,\mathbf{W})]} \mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}[(T,i,j,\mathbf{W})]} \mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}[(T,i,j,\mathbf{W})]} \mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}[(T,i,j,\mathbf{W})]} \mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}[(T,i,j,\mathbf{W})]} \mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}[(T,i,j,\mathbf{W})]} \mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}[(T,i,j,\mathbf{W})]} \mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}[(T,i,j,\mathbf{W})]} \mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}[(T,i,j,\mathbf{W})]} \mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}[(T,i,j,\mathbf{W})]} \mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}[(T,i,j,\mathbf{W})]} \mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}[(T,i,j,\mathbf{W})]} \mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}[(T,i,j,\mathbf{W})]} \mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}[(T,i,j,\mathbf{W})]} \mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}[(T,i,j,\mathbf{W})]} \mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}[(T,i,j,\mathbf{W})]} \mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}[(T,i,j,\mathbf{W})]} \mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}[(T,i,j,\mathbf{W})]} \mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}[(T,i,j,\mathbf{W})]} \mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}[(T,i,j,\mathbf{W})]} \mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}[(T,i,j,\mathbf{W})]} \mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}[(T,i,j,\mathbf{W})]} \mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}[(T,i,j,\mathbf{W})]} \mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}[(T,i,j,\mathbf{W})]} \mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}[(T,i,j,\mathbf{W})]} \mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}[(T,i,j,\mathbf{W})]} \mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}[(T,i,j,\mathbf{W})]} \mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}[(T,i,j,\mathbf{W})]} \mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}[(T,i,j,\mathbf{W})]} \mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}[(T,i,j,\mathbf{W})]} \mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}[(T,i,j,\mathbf{W})]} \mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}[(T,i,j,\mathbf{W})]} \mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}[(T,i,j,\mathbf{W})]} \mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}[(T,i,j,\mathbf{W})]} \mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}[(T,i,j,\mathbf{W})]} \mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}[(T,i,j,\mathbf{W})]} \mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}[(T,i,j,\mathbf{W})]} \mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}[(T,i,j,\mathbf{W})]} \mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}[(T,i,j,\mathbf{W})]} \mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}[(T,i,j,\mathbf{W})]} \mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}[(T,i,j,\mathbf{W})]} \mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}[(T,i,j,\mathbf{W})]} \mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}[(T,i,j,\mathbf{W})]} \mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}[(T,i,j,\mathbf{W})]} \mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}[(T,i,j,\mathbf{W})]} \mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}[(T,i,j,\mathbf{W})]} \mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}[(T,i,j,\mathbf{W})]} \mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}[(T,i,j,\mathbf{W})]} \mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}[(T,i,j,\mathbf{W})]} \mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}[(T,i,j,\mathbf{W})]} \mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}[(T,i,j,\mathbf{W})]} \mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}[(T,i,j,\mathbf{W})]} \mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}[(T,i,j,\mathbf{W})]} \mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}[(T,i,j,\mathbf{W})]} \mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}[(T,i,j,\mathbf{W})]} \mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}[(T,i,j,\mathbf{W})]} \mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}[(T,i,j,$ 

In the table above, "?" is either nothing or "temp", i.e., if the values are set in both non-temporary slots and temporary slots, they are the same. Note that  $\mathbf{r}_f - \mathbf{r}_f[q]\mathbf{e}_q$  is simply  $\mathbf{r}_f$  with its  $q^{\text{th}}$  entry changed to 0, whence  $\mathbf{r}_f[q]$  does not appear. The compensation is governed by the following identity:

<span id="page-63-0"></span>
$$\begin{split} \ell_{t',i,j,\mathbf{W},q'} &= -\mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}}[(t'-1,i,j,\mathbf{W})]\mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{f}}[q'] + \sum_{\tau \in \mathcal{T}} \mathbf{c}_{\tau}(\mathbf{x};t',i,j,\mathbf{W};\mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}})(\mathbf{M}_{\tau}(\mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{f}} - \mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{f}}[q]\mathbf{e}_{q} + \mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{f}}[q]\mathbf{e}_{q}))[q'] \\ &= -\mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}}[(t'-1,i,j,\mathbf{W})]\mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{f}}[q'] + \sum_{\tau \in \mathcal{T}} \mathbf{c}_{\tau}(\mathbf{x};t',i,j,\mathbf{W};\mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}}) \cdot (\mathbf{M}_{\tau}(\mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{f}} - \mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{f}}[q]\mathbf{e}_{q}))[q'] \\ &+ \sum_{\tau \in \mathcal{T}} \mathbf{c}_{\tau}(\mathbf{x};t',i,j,\mathbf{W};\mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}})\mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{f}}[q] \cdot (\mathbf{M}_{\tau}\mathbf{e}_{q})[q']. \end{split}$$

In this iteration, the *modes* of  $\ell_{t',i,j,\mathbf{W},q'}$  are...

$$q' < q \qquad q' = q \qquad q' > q$$

$$t' < t \qquad S \qquad S \rightarrow SC \rightarrow S \qquad S$$

$$t' = t \qquad ST \qquad \boxed{HT \rightarrow HW \rightarrow RW \rightarrow SW \rightarrow ST} HT \rightarrow HCT \rightarrow HT$$

$$t' > t \quad H \rightarrow HC \rightarrow H \qquad H \rightarrow HC \rightarrow H$$

The shorthands are Honest, Random, Simulated, Compensated, hard Wired, Temporary. For three-mode chains, the middle one spans  $\mathsf{H}^b_{3,t,3,q,2\sim4}$ .

The net effect is that  $\ell_{t,i,j,\mathbf{W},q}$ 's change from honest and temporary to simulated and temporary.

Figure 9 (continued) — Notes.

• <u>Hybrid H</u><sup>b</sup><sub>3,t,3,q,5</sub> proceeds identically to H<sup>b</sup><sub>3,t,3,q,4</sub>, except that all occurrences of  $\mathbf{r}_{\mathrm{f}}[q]$  and  $\mathbf{s}_{\mathrm{f}}[q]$  are moved back to  $\mathbf{v}_{q'}$ 's (including putting  $\mathbf{s}_{\mathrm{f}}[q]$  back to  $\mathbf{v}_{q}[\mathsf{sim}]$ ) — compensation is undone — and that some clean-up work is done to prepare for the next iteration. More specifically, the clean-up work involves clearing the values of  $\mathbf{v}_{q}$ ,  $\mathbf{u}_{t,i,j,\mathbf{W}}$  at  $\mathsf{sim}^{\mathsf{comp}}$  for all  $i,j,\mathbf{W}$  and putting  $\mathbf{s}_{\mathrm{f}}[q]$  into  $\mathbf{v}_{q}[\mathsf{sim}^{\mathsf{temp}}]$ . As a result, all the labels lose their compensated mode, and the labels  $\ell_{t,i,j,\mathbf{W},q}$  for all  $i,j,\mathbf{W}$  become simulated and temporary. Note that  $\mathsf{H}^b_{3,t,3,q,5} \equiv \mathsf{H}^b_{3,t,3,q+1,1}$ .

Lastly, observe that  $\mathsf{H}^b_{3,t,3,1,1} \equiv \mathsf{H}^b_{3,t,2}$  and  $\mathsf{H}^b_{3,t,3,Q,5} \equiv \mathsf{H}^b_{3,t,4}$ . By a hybrid argument over the inner loop hybrids, we have  $\mathsf{H}^b_{3,t,2} \approx \mathsf{H}^b_{3,t,4}$ .

Hybriding over the outer loop hybrids yields  $\mathsf{H}_2^b \approx \mathsf{H}_4^b$  in Case 2.

<u>Remarks.</u> For the version based on  $MDDH_k$ , the labels are simulated as

$$\ell_{t,i,j,\mathbf{W},q} = (\mathbf{S}_{\mathbf{x}}^{\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{S}_{\mathbf{f}})[(t,i,j,\mathbf{W}),q] \quad \text{for} \quad \mathbf{S}_{\mathbf{x}} \overset{\hspace{0.1em}\mathsf{\scriptscriptstyle\$}}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_p^{[k]\times([T+1]\times[N]\times[S]\times\{0,1\}^S)}, \ \mathbf{S}_{\mathbf{f}} \overset{\hspace{0.1em}\mathsf{\scriptscriptstyle\$}}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_p^{k\times Q}.$$

The proof for Case 1 goes by invoking  $MDDH_k$  instead of DDH. We discuss the change in the proof for Case 2. At some point, we need to switch the randomizers of the labels with some specific t, q to truly random. Invoking  $MDDH_k$  apparently requires completely removing the  $q^{th}$  column of  $\mathbf{R}_f$ , yet this column is used to compute the randomizers for the labels with q' = q that are still honest. We got away with this when assuming DDH because both distributions give us access to  $\mathbf{r}_f[q]$  (a convenient shortcut), i.e.,

$$\begin{split} & \left[ \left[ \mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}}[(t-1, \mathbf{u}, \mathbf{u}, \mathbf{u})], \mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{f}}[q], \mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}}[(t-1, \mathbf{u}, \mathbf{u}, \mathbf{u})] \mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{f}}[q] \right] \right]_{1} \\ & (\mathrm{DDH}) \quad \approx \left[ \left[ \mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}}[(t-1, \mathbf{u}, \mathbf{u}, \mathbf{u}, \mathbf{u})], \mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{f}}[q], \quad \mathbf{r}[(t-1, \mathbf{u}, \mathbf{u}, \mathbf{u}, \mathbf{u}, q)] \quad \right] \right]_{1}. \end{split}$$

A naïve attempt to generalize the proof to work with  $MDDH_k$  is to say

$$\begin{bmatrix} \mathbf{R}_{\mathbf{x}}[\mathbf{u},(t-1,\mathbf{u},\mathbf{u},\mathbf{u})], \mathbf{R}_{\mathbf{f}}[\mathbf{u},q], (\mathbf{R}_{\mathbf{x}}[\mathbf{u},(t-1,\mathbf{u},\mathbf{u},\mathbf{u})])^{\mathsf{T}} \mathbf{R}_{\mathbf{f}}[\mathbf{u},q] \end{bmatrix}_{1}$$

$$\stackrel{??}{\approx} \begin{bmatrix} \mathbf{R}_{\mathbf{x}}[\mathbf{u},(t-1,\mathbf{u},\mathbf{u},\mathbf{u})], \mathbf{R}_{\mathbf{f}}[\mathbf{u},q], \qquad \mathbf{r}[(t-1,\mathbf{u},\mathbf{u},\mathbf{u}),q] \end{bmatrix}_{1},$$

which does not follow by  $MDDH_k$  (and is false for symmetric pairing groups). The correct proof uses

$$(\text{MDDH}_{k}) \approx \begin{bmatrix} \mathbf{R}_{\mathbf{x}}[\boldsymbol{\square}, (\boldsymbol{\square}, \boldsymbol{\square}, \boldsymbol{\square}, \boldsymbol{\square})], & \mathbf{r}[(\mathbf{R}_{\mathbf{x}}[\boldsymbol{\square}, (t'-1, \boldsymbol{\square}, \boldsymbol{\square}, \boldsymbol{\square})])^{\mathsf{T}} \mathbf{R}_{\mathbf{f}}[\boldsymbol{\square}, q] \}_{t'>t}, & \mathbf{r}[(t-1, \boldsymbol{\square}, \boldsymbol{\square}, \boldsymbol{\square}), q] \end{bmatrix}_{1}$$

$$(\text{MDDH}_{k}) \approx \begin{bmatrix} \mathbf{R}_{\mathbf{x}}[\boldsymbol{\square}, (\boldsymbol{\square}, \boldsymbol{\square}, \boldsymbol{\square}, \boldsymbol{\square})], & \mathbf{r}[(t'-1, \boldsymbol{\square}, \boldsymbol{\square}, \boldsymbol{\square})] \end{bmatrix}_{1}^{\mathsf{T}} \mathbf{R}_{\mathbf{f}}[\boldsymbol{\square}, q] \}_{t'>t}, & \mathbf{r}[(t-1, \boldsymbol{\square}, \boldsymbol{\square}, \boldsymbol{\square}, \boldsymbol{\square}, q)] \end{bmatrix}_{1}$$

$$(\text{MDDH}_{k}) \approx \begin{bmatrix} \mathbf{R}_{\mathbf{x}}[\boldsymbol{\square}, (\boldsymbol{\square}, \boldsymbol{\square}, \boldsymbol{\square}, \boldsymbol{\square})], & \mathbf{r}[(t'-1, \boldsymbol{\square}, \boldsymbol{\square}, \boldsymbol{\square}, \boldsymbol{\square}, \boldsymbol{\square})] \end{bmatrix}_{1}^{\mathsf{T}} \mathbf{R}_{\mathbf{f}}[\boldsymbol{\square}, q] \}_{t'>t}, & \mathbf{r}[(t-1, \boldsymbol{\square}, \boldsymbol{\square}, \boldsymbol{\square}, \boldsymbol{\square}, q)] \end{bmatrix}_{1}$$

In other words, we first switch all the randomizers of the labels with q' = q to truly random, then switch back the randomizers of the labels with t' > t, q' = q to pseudorandom (the randomizers for the labels with t' < t are already gone in that iteration, because those labels are already simulated). A similar strategy is used for  $\mathbf{S}_{\mathbf{x}}$ ,  $\mathbf{S}_{\mathbf{f}}$  when we switch the truly random labels to pseudorandom simulated ones.

#### <span id="page-64-0"></span>7.3 KP-ABE for L

We use the same technique in Section 6.3 to convert 1-ABE for L into a full-fledged ABE for L. The only difference is that we will need two copies of the indices in the private slot.

In the security proof of KP-ABE for ABPs, the private slot can be thought as a compartment isolating the interaction between all the secret keys and the challenge ciphertext from the other ciphertexts (which can be generated by the adversary using the master public key in the public slot). All the secret keys can share the same private slot because the security of 1-ABE for ABPs is unaffected by the extra keys. However, the security of 1-ABE for L does not automatically extend to the multi-key setting, and we need an extra copy of the indices to further isolate the interaction between the challenge ciphertext and the secret key being modified from the other secret keys.

<span id="page-65-0"></span>Construction 37 (KP-ABE for L). We describe the construction for any fixed value of the security parameter  $\lambda$  and suppress the appearance of  $\lambda$  below for simplicity of notations. Let the function class be

$$\mathcal{F} = \{ M|_{N,T,S} : \mathbb{Z}_p^N \to \mathbb{Z}_p \mid M \in \mathsf{TM}, N, T, S \ge 1, p \text{ prime} \}.$$

Let (Garble, Eval) be the AKGS for  $\mathcal{F}$  in Construction 30,  $\mathcal{G}$  pairing groups of order p, and (IPFE.Setup, IPFE.KeyGen, IPFE.Enc, IPFE.Dec) a slotted IPFE based on  $\mathcal{G}$ . We construct an ABE scheme for the following singleton predicate space  $\mathcal{P}$ :

$$X = \{(\mathbf{x}, 1^T, 1^{2^S}) \mid \mathbf{x} \in \{0, 1\}^N \text{ for some } N \ge 1, T, S \ge 1\}, \quad Y = \mathsf{TM},$$

$$P : X \times Y \to \{0, 1\}, ((\mathbf{x}, 1^T, 1^{2^S}), M) \mapsto M|_{N, T, S}(\mathbf{x}) \text{ for } \mathbf{x} \in \{0, 1\}^N,$$

$$\mathcal{P} = \{P\}.$$

The ABE scheme (Setup, KeyGen, Enc, Dec) operates as follows:

• Setup(P) takes the only predicate as input. It generates IPFE master public/secret key pair (msk, mpk)  $\stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow}$  IPFE.Setup( $\mathfrak{s}_{\text{pub}}, \mathfrak{s}_{\text{priv}}$ ) for the following slots:

$$\begin{split} &\mathfrak{s}_{\mathrm{pub}} = \left\{\mathsf{pad^{ct}}, \mathsf{pad^{sk}}, \mathsf{init^{\mathrm{pub}}}, \mathsf{rand^{\mathrm{pub}}}, \mathsf{acc^{\mathrm{pub}}}\right\} \cup \left\{\mathsf{tb^{\mathrm{pub}}_{\tau}} \,\middle|\, \tau \in \mathcal{T}\right\}, \\ &\mathfrak{s}_{\mathrm{copy}} = \left\{\mathsf{init^{\mathrm{copy}}}, \mathsf{rand^{\mathrm{copy}}}, \mathsf{acc^{\mathrm{copy}}}\right\} \cup \left\{\mathsf{tb^{\mathrm{copy}}_{\tau}} \,\middle|\, \tau \in \mathcal{T}\right\}, \\ &\mathfrak{s}_{\mathrm{priv}} = \mathfrak{s}_{\mathrm{copy}} \cup \mathfrak{s}_{\text{1-ABE}} \cup \left\{\mathsf{pad^{\mathrm{copy}}}, \mathsf{pad^{\mathrm{temp}}}\right\}, \end{split}$$

where  $\mathfrak{s}_{\text{1-ABE}}$  is the index set defined in Construction 33. The algorithm returns (mpk, msk) as the master public/secret key pair.

Note: The indices  $pad^{ct}$ ,  $pad^{sk}$  are used to compute  $h + \mu$  in the exponent, where h (resp.  $\mu$ ) is the random pad in ct (resp. sk) embedded at  $pad^{ct}$  (resp.  $pad^{sk}$ ). The values in  $\mathfrak{s}_{priv}$  are set to 0 by the honest algorithms and reserved for the security proof. The names of the other indices follow the convention in 1-ABE.

• KeyGen(msk, M) takes the master secret key and a Turing machine  $M = (Q, \mathbf{y}_{acc}, \delta) \in \mathsf{TM} = Y$  as input. It computes the transition blocks  $\mathbf{M}_{\tau}$  for  $\tau \in \mathcal{T}$  from  $\delta$ , samples  $\mu \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_p, \mathbf{r}_f \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_p^Q$ , and sets the vectors  $\mathbf{v}_{pad}, \mathbf{v}_{init}$  and  $\mathbf{v}_q \in \mathbb{Z}_p^{\mathfrak{s}}$  for  $q \in [Q]$  as follows:

| vector                                                                                 | pad <sup>ct</sup> | pad <sup>sk</sup> | $init^{\mathrm{pub}}$        | $rand^{\mathrm{pub}}$         | $acc^{\mathrm{pub}}$               | $tb^\mathrm{pub}_\tau$                               | $ \inf \mathfrak{s}_{\mathrm{priv}} $ |
|----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|-------------------|-------------------|------------------------------|-------------------------------|------------------------------------|------------------------------------------------------|---------------------------------------|
| $\mathbf{v}_{\mathrm{pad}}$                                                            | 1                 | $\mu$             | 0                            | 0                             | 0                                  | 0                                                    |                                       |
| $\begin{aligned} \mathbf{v}_{\mathrm{pad}} \ \mathbf{v}_{\mathrm{init}} \end{aligned}$ | 0                 | 0                 | $\mathbf{r}_{\mathrm{f}}[1]$ | 0                             | 0                                  | 0                                                    | 0                                     |
| $\mathbf{v}_q$                                                                         | 0                 | 0                 | 0                            | $-\mathbf{r}_{\mathrm{f}}[q]$ | $\mu \mathbf{y}_{\mathrm{acc}}[q]$ | $0 \\ (\mathbf{M}_{\tau}\mathbf{r}_{\mathrm{f}})[q]$ |                                       |

The algorithm generates an IPFE secret key for each vector defined above:

$$\begin{split} \mathsf{isk}_{\mathrm{pad}} & \overset{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathsf{IPFE}.\mathsf{KeyGen}(\mathsf{msk}, \llbracket \mathbf{v}_{\mathrm{pad}} \rrbracket_2), \\ \mathsf{isk}_{\mathrm{init}} & \overset{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathsf{IPFE}.\mathsf{KeyGen}(\mathsf{msk}, \llbracket \mathbf{v}_{\mathrm{init}} \rrbracket_2), \\ \mathsf{for} \ q \in [Q] \colon & \mathsf{isk}_q & \overset{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathsf{IPFE}.\mathsf{KeyGen}(\mathsf{msk}, \llbracket \mathbf{v}_q \rrbracket_2). \end{split}$$

It returns  $\mathsf{sk} = (\mathsf{isk}_{\mathsf{pad}}, M, \mathsf{isk}_{\mathsf{init}}, \mathsf{isk}_1, \dots, \mathsf{isk}_Q).$ 

Note: Same as in 1-ABE for L, KeyGen creates the garbling with secrets  $\alpha = \mu, \beta = 0$ .

• Enc(mpk,  $(\mathbf{x}, 1^T, 1^{2^S}), g$ ) takes the master public key, an input  $\mathbf{x} \in \{0, 1\}^N$  for some  $N \ge 1$ , time/space complexity bounds  $T, S \ge 1$  (encoded as  $1^T$  and  $1^{2^S}$ ), and a message  $g \in M = G_T$  as input. It samples  $h \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_p, s \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_p, \mathbf{r}_\mathbf{x} \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_p^{[0..T] \times [N] \times [S] \times \{0,1\}^S}$  and sets the vectors  $\mathbf{u}_{\text{pad}}, \mathbf{u}_{\text{init}}$  and  $\mathbf{u}_{t,i,j,\mathbf{W}} \in \mathbb{Z}_p^{\mathfrak{s}_{\text{pub}}}$  for  $t \in [T+1], i \in [N], j \in [S], \mathbf{W} \in \{0,1\}^S$  as follows:

| vector                                                                                 | pad <sup>ct</sup>                      | pad <sup>sk</sup> | init <sup>pub</sup>                                                        | the other indices |
|----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|----------------------------------------|-------------------|----------------------------------------------------------------------------|-------------------|
| $\begin{aligned} \mathbf{u}_{\mathrm{pad}} \ \mathbf{u}_{\mathrm{init}} \end{aligned}$ | $\begin{pmatrix} h \\ 0 \end{pmatrix}$ | $s \\ 0$          | $\begin{bmatrix} 0 \\ s\mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}}[(0,1,1,0_S)] \end{bmatrix}$ | 0                 |

| vector                                                                         | $rand^{\mathrm{pub}}$                                                                                                          | $acc^{\mathrm{pub}}$ | $tb^{\mathrm{pub}}_\tau$                                                                            | the other indices |
|--------------------------------------------------------------------------------|--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|----------------------|-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|-------------------|
| $t \leq T$ : $\mathbf{u}_{t,i,j,\mathbf{W}}$ $\mathbf{u}_{T+1,i,j,\mathbf{W}}$ | $\begin{vmatrix} s\mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}}[(t-1,i,j,\mathbf{W})] \\ s\mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}}[(T,i,j,\mathbf{W})] \end{vmatrix}$ | $0 \\ s$             | $sc_{\tau}(\mathbf{x};t,i,j,\mathbf{W};\mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}}) \begin{vmatrix} \\ 0 \end{vmatrix}$ | 0                 |

The algorithm then generates IPFE ciphertexts for the vectors defined above:

$$\begin{split} & \mathsf{ict}_{\mathrm{pad}} \overset{\hspace{0.1em}\mathsf{\scriptscriptstyle\$}}{\leftarrow} \mathsf{IPFE}.\mathsf{SlotEnc}(\mathsf{mpk}, \llbracket \mathbf{u}_{\mathrm{pad}} \rrbracket_1), \qquad \mathsf{ict}_{\mathrm{init}} \overset{\hspace{0.1em}\mathsf{\scriptscriptstyle\$}}{\leftarrow} \mathsf{IPFE}.\mathsf{SlotEnc}(\mathsf{mpk}, \llbracket \mathbf{u}_{\mathrm{init}} \rrbracket_1), \\ & \mathsf{for} \ t \in [T+1], i \in [N], j \in [S], \mathbf{W} \in \{0,1\}^S \colon \ \mathsf{ict}_{t,i,j,\mathbf{W}} \overset{\hspace{0.1em}\mathsf{\scriptscriptstyle\$}}{\leftarrow} \mathsf{IPFE}.\mathsf{SlotEnc}(\mathsf{mpk}, \llbracket \mathbf{u}_{t,i,j,\mathbf{W}} \rrbracket_1). \\ & \mathsf{It} \ \mathsf{returns} \ \mathsf{ct} = \left(g + \llbracket h \rrbracket_{\mathrm{T}}, \mathsf{ict}_{\mathrm{pad}}, (\mathbf{x}, T, S), \mathsf{ict}_{\mathrm{init}}, (\mathsf{ict}_{t,i,j,\mathbf{W}})_{t \in [T+1], i \in [N], j \in [S], \mathbf{W} \in \{0,1\}^S}\right). \end{split}$$

• Dec(sk, ct) takes a secret key sk and a ciphertext ct as input. It parses

$$\begin{split} &\mathsf{sk} \ \mathsf{as} \ \left(\mathsf{isk}_{\mathrm{pad}}, M, \mathsf{isk}_{\mathrm{init}}, \mathsf{isk}_1, \dots, \mathsf{isk}_Q\right) \quad \mathsf{and} \\ &\mathsf{ct} \ \mathsf{as} \ \left([\![z]\!]_T, \mathsf{ict}_{\mathrm{pad}}, (\mathbf{x}, T, S), \mathsf{ict}_{\mathrm{init}}, (\mathsf{ict}_{t,i,j,\mathbf{W}})_{t \in [T+1], i \in [N], j \in [S], \mathbf{W} \in \{0,1\}^S}\right), \end{split}$$

where  $M = (Q, \mathbf{y}_{acc}, \delta) \in \mathsf{TM}$  and  $\mathbf{x} \in \{0, 1\}^N$ . The algorithm returns  $\bot$  if  $M|_{N,T,S}(\mathbf{x}) = 0$ . Otherwise, it does the following (recall that  $\mathcal{C}_{M,N,S} = [N] \times [S] \times \{0, 1\}^S \times [Q]$ ):

$$\begin{split} & \quad \|z'\|_{\mathrm{T}} \leftarrow \mathsf{IPFE.Dec}(\mathsf{isk}_{\mathrm{pad}}, \mathsf{ict}_{\mathrm{pad}}), \quad \|\ell_{\mathrm{init}}\|_{\mathrm{T}} \leftarrow \mathsf{IPFE.Dec}(\mathsf{isk}_{\mathrm{init}}, \mathsf{ict}_{\mathrm{init}}), \\ & \text{for } t \in [T+1], (i,j,\mathbf{W},q) \in \mathcal{C}_{M,N,S} \colon \quad \|\ell_{t,i,j,\mathbf{W},q}\|_{\mathrm{T}} \leftarrow \mathsf{IPFE.Dec}(\mathsf{isk}_q, \mathsf{ict}_{t,i,j,\mathbf{W}}), \\ & \quad \|\mu'\|_{\mathrm{T}} \leftarrow \mathsf{Eval}\big((M,1^N,1^T,1^{2^S},p),\mathbf{x}, \|\ell_{\mathrm{init}}\|_{\mathrm{T}}, (\|\ell_{t,z}\|_{\mathrm{T}})_{t \in [T+1], z \in \mathcal{C}_{M,N,S}}\big). \end{split}$$

The algorithm returns  $[\![z]\!]_T + [\![\mu']\!]_T - [\![z']\!]_T$  as the decrypted message.

Note: By combining the arguments for the correctness of 1-ABE for L (Construction 33) and KP-ABE for ABPs (Construction 26), it is readily verified that  $\mu' = s\mu M|_{N,T,S}(\mathbf{x}) = s\mu$  and  $z' = h + s\mu$ . Therefore,  $[\![z]\!]_T + [\![\mu']\!]_T - [\![z']\!]_T = g + [\![h]\!]_T + [\![s\mu]\!]_T - [\![h + s\mu]\!]_T = g$ , i.e., Dec correctly recovers the message.

<span id="page-67-0"></span>**Theorem 38.** Suppose in Construction 37, the SXDH assumption holds in  $\mathcal{G}$  and the slotted IPFE is function-hiding, then the construction is a secure ABE scheme.

<u>Proof.</u> Let  $\mathcal{A}$  be any efficient adversary. We want to show that the distinguishing advantage of  $\mathcal{A}$  against  $\mathsf{Exp}^0_{\mathsf{CPA}}$  and  $\mathsf{Exp}^1_{\mathsf{CPA}}$  is negligible. Suppose  $\mathcal{A}$  makes  $\Phi$  secret key queries, it receives  $\mathsf{sk}_{\varphi}$  encoding half a garbling for machine  $M_{\varphi}$  in the public slot and ct encrypting message  $g_b$  and encoding half a garbling for input string  $\mathbf{x} \in \{0,1\}^N$  and time/space bounds T,S in the public slot, where  $M_{\varphi}$ 's,  $\mathbf{x}, T, S$  are chosen adaptively by  $\mathcal{A}$  subject to the constraint that  $M_{\varphi}|_{N,T,S}(\mathbf{x}) = 0$  for all  $\varphi \in [\Phi]$ . The goal of the proof is thus to show the message  $g_b$  is computationally hidden.

At a high level, the proof involves three steps, similar to those in the proof of IND-CPA security of KP-ABE for ABPs (Theorem 27):

- First, the garblings (in both ct and  $\mathsf{sk}_{\varphi}$ ) as well as the secret key pads  $\mu_{\varphi}$  are removed from  $\mathfrak{s}_{\mathrm{pub}}$ . Instead, ct embeds in  $\mathfrak{s}_{\mathrm{copy}}$  (half of) the garbling without s, and each  $\mathsf{sk}_{\varphi}$  embeds in  $\mathfrak{s}_{\mathrm{copy}}$  (half) a garbling generated with pad  $\widehat{\mu}_{\varphi}^0$  and randomness  $\widehat{\mathbf{r}}_{\varphi,\mathrm{f}}$  independent of those in  $\mathfrak{s}_{\mathrm{pub}}$ .
- Next, we go through a loop of  $\Phi$  iterations. In the  $\varphi^{\text{th}}$  iteration, we replace  $\widehat{\mu}_{\varphi}^{0}$  in  $\mathbf{v}_{\varphi,\text{pad}}$  by an independent random value  $\widehat{\mu}_{\varphi}^{1}$  (inconsistent with  $\widehat{\mu}_{\varphi}^{0}$  used to generate  $\mathbf{v}_{\varphi,\text{init}}$  and  $\mathbf{v}_{\varphi,q}$ 's). However, this is not as simple as the case of KP-ABE for ABPs, because the security of 1-ABE for L (Theorem 34) does not automatically generalize to the case of multiple secret key queries, which can be regarded as a consequence of reusing the randomness in the ciphertext vectors. We employ the trick of temporary mode to resolve the problem. Roughly speaking,  $\mathfrak{s}_{\text{1-ABE}}$  is used for the interaction between  $\mathsf{sk}_{\varphi}$  (the secret key being modified) and  $\mathsf{ct}$ , while  $\mathfrak{s}_{\text{copy}}$  is used for the interaction between all other secret keys and  $\mathsf{ct}$ . The ciphertext uses two sets of independent randomness  $\mathbf{r}_{x}$  in  $\mathfrak{s}_{\text{copy}}$  and  $\widehat{\mathbf{r}}_{x}$  in  $\mathfrak{s}_{\text{1-ABE}}$  so that the proof of Theorem 34 can be invoked in  $\mathfrak{s}_{\text{1-ABE}}$ .
- When all the secret keys have their pads  $\widehat{\mu}_{\varphi}^{0}$  replaced by  $\widehat{\mu}_{\varphi}^{1}$ , we move the random pad h from the ciphertext into all the secret keys, by which point h will be perfectly hidden by the pads  $\widehat{\mu}_{\varphi}^{1}$  and perfectly hide the message.

We start with the first step, which is the first step in Theorem 27 with DDH instead of MDDH:

- <u>Hybrid H</u><sup>b</sup><sub>0</sub> proceeds identically to Exp<sup>b</sup><sub>CPA</sub>, where the ict's (in ct) are generated using SlotEnc.
   In Figure 10, this is depicted as "⊥" in the u's.
- <u>Hybrid  $H_1^b$ </u> proceeds identically to  $H_0^b$ , except that the ict's are generated using Enc with  $\mathbf{u}|_{\mathfrak{S}_{\text{priv}}}$  set to **0**. By the slot-mode correctness of the slotted IPFE, we have  $H_1^b \equiv H_0^b$ .
- <u>Hybrid  $H_2^b$ </u> proceeds identically to  $H_1^b$ , except with how the (secret key) pads and the labels are computed (as inner products) is changed instead of multiplying with s in the ciphertext, s is multiplied in the secret key (which prepares the secret key randomness to be rerandomized):
  - In the ciphertext vectors, values at  $pad^{sk}$ ,  $init^{pub}$ ,  $rand^{pub}$ ,  $acc^{pub}$  and  $tb_{\tau}^{pub}$ 's (in the public slot) are moved to  $pad^{copy}$ ,  $\mathfrak{s}_{copy}$  (in the private slot), and the multiplier s is removed.
  - In the secret key vectors, values at  $pad^{sk}$ ,  $init^{pub}$ ,  $rand^{pub}$ ,  $acc^{pub}$  and  $tb_{\tau}^{pub}$ 's (in the public slot) are copied to  $pad^{copy}$ ,  $\mathfrak{s}_{copy}$  (in the private slot), and s is multiplied to the copy in the private slot.

For brevity, the vectors for computing the labels are not spelled out. The shorthand " $\propto \mathbf{z}$ " means that the components there are linear in  $\mathbf{z}$  and efficiently computable given  $\mathbf{z}$  in the exponent, and that there is only one natural way of computing them (cf. Construction 37).

Figure 10: The first/last few hybrids in the proof of IND-CPA security of our KP-ABE scheme for L.

The hybrid is illustrated in Figure 10. Since the inner products remain the same and the secret key vectors have their values in the public slot unchanged, we have  $\mathsf{H}^b_2 \approx \mathsf{H}^b_1$  by the function-hiding property of IPFE. An alternative view of this hybrid is that in each secret key  $\mathsf{sk}_{\varphi}$ , two (half) garblings are embedded, one generated for  $\mu_{\varphi}$  using randomness  $\mathbf{r}_{\varphi,\mathrm{f}}$  in the public slot, the other generated for  $s\mu_{\varphi}$  using randomness  $s\mathbf{r}_{\varphi,\mathrm{f}}$  in the private slot.

• <u>Hybrid H</u><sup>b</sup><sub>3</sub> proceeds identically to H<sup>b</sup><sub>2</sub>, except that the garbling in the private slots of the secret key vectors are generated for independent pad  $\widehat{\mu}^0_{\varphi}$  with independent randomness  $\widehat{\mathbf{r}}_{\varphi,f}$ . Note that the only difference between H<sup>b</sup><sub>2</sub> and H<sup>b</sup><sub>3</sub> is that in the former, the randomness and the pads of the garblings in the private slot are *random multiples* of those in the public slot, and that in the latter, those in the private slot are independently sampled. The DDH assumption in  $G_2$  says

$$\left\{[\![\mu_{\varphi},\mathbf{r}_{\varphi,\mathbf{f}};\,s\mu_{\varphi},s\mathbf{r}_{\varphi,\mathbf{f}}]\!]_2\right\}_{\varphi\in[\Phi]}\approx \left\{[\![\mu_{\varphi},\mathbf{r}_{\varphi,\mathbf{f}};\,\widehat{\mu}_{\varphi}^0,\widehat{\mathbf{r}}_{\varphi,\mathbf{f}}]\!]_2\right\}_{\varphi\in[\Phi]}.$$

Given  $[\![\mu_{\varphi}, \mathbf{r}_{\varphi,f}]\!]_2$  and either  $[\![s\mu_{\varphi}, s\mathbf{r}_{\varphi,f}]\!]_2$  or  $[\![\widehat{\mu}^0_{\varphi}, \widehat{\mathbf{r}}_{\varphi,f}]\!]_2$ , the secret key vectors can be efficiently computed in the exponent, and everything else can be efficiently computed. Therefore,  $\mathsf{H}^b_2 \approx \mathsf{H}^b_3$  by the DDH assumption in  $G_2$ .

We have completed the first step of the proof. Now we proceed to the second step, in which we switch  $\widehat{\mu}_{\varphi}^0$  to independent random values  $\widehat{\mu}_{\varphi}^1$  (inconsistent with  $\mathbf{v}_{\varphi,\mathrm{init}}$  and  $\mathbf{v}_{\varphi,q}$ 's) one by one:

• <u>Hybrid  $H_{4,\varphi}^b$ </u> proceeds identically to  $H_3^b$ , except that for  $\varphi' < \varphi$  (the first  $\varphi - 1$  secret keys),  $\mathbf{v}_{\varphi',\mathrm{pad}}$  (in  $\mathsf{isk}_{\varphi',\mathrm{pad}}$ ) stores an independent random value  $\widehat{\mu}_{\varphi}^1 \stackrel{\hspace{0.1em}\mathsf{\scriptscriptstyle\$}}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_p$  at  $\mathsf{pad}^{\mathrm{copy}}$ .

Observe that  $\mathsf{H}^b_{4,1} \equiv \mathsf{H}^b_3$ . We show  $\mathsf{H}^b_{4,\varphi} \approx \mathsf{H}^b_{4,\varphi+1}$  for all  $\varphi \in [\Phi], b \in \{0,1\}$  as a separate claim:

<span id="page-69-0"></span>Claim 39. 
$$\mathsf{H}^b_{4,\varphi} \approx \mathsf{H}^b_{4,\varphi+1} \ for \ all \ \varphi \in [\Phi], b \in \{0,1\}.$$

For now, we focus on the last step:

• <u>Hybrid H</u><sup>b</sup><sub>5</sub> proceeds identically to H<sup>b</sup><sub>3</sub>, except that all the pads  $\widehat{\mu}_{\varphi}^{0}$  in  $\mathbf{v}_{\varphi,\mathrm{pad}}[\mathsf{pad}^{\mathrm{copy}}]$  are replaced by independent random values  $\widehat{\mu}_{\varphi}^{1} \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_{p}$ . The hybrid is shown in Figure 10. Observe that H<sup>b</sup><sub>5</sub>  $\equiv$  H<sup>b</sup><sub>4,\Phi+1</sub>.

Note that in this hybrid, the inner products of  $\mathbf{u}_{pad}$  and  $\mathbf{v}_{\varphi,pad}$ 's are  $h + \widehat{\mu}_{\varphi}^1$ , which hide h. However, h still appears in  $\mathbf{u}_{pad}$ . In the next hybrid, we remove h from  $\mathbf{u}_{pad}$  and directly hardwire the inner products  $h + \widehat{\mu}_{\varphi}^1$  in  $\mathbf{v}_{\varphi,pad}$ 's so that h becomes information-theoretically hidden.

• <u>Hybrid H</u><sup>b</sup><sub>6</sub> proceeds identically to H<sup>b</sup><sub>5</sub>, except that the random pad h is removed from  $\mathbf{u}_{pad}[\mathsf{pad}^{\mathsf{ct}}]$  and all the  $\mathbf{v}_{\varphi,pad}$  stores  $h + \widehat{\mu}^1_{\varphi}$  at  $\mathsf{pad}^{\mathsf{copy}}$ . Since the inner products and the public slot of the secret key vectors remain unchanged, we have H<sup>b</sup><sub>5</sub>  $\approx$  H<sup>b</sup><sub>6</sub> by the function-hiding property of IPFE.

We have  $\mathsf{H}_6^0 \equiv \mathsf{H}_6^1$  because h is perfectly hidden by each  $\widehat{\mu}_{\varphi}^1$  and perfectly hides the message. Therefore, by a hybrid argument, we conclude  $\mathsf{Exp}_{\mathrm{CPA}}^0 \approx \mathsf{Exp}_{\mathrm{CPA}}^1$ .

<u>Proof\_(Claim 39).</u> Fix some  $\varphi \in [\Phi]$ ,  $b \in \{0,1\}$  and we want to show  $\mathsf{H}^b_{4,\varphi} \approx \mathsf{H}^b_{4,\varphi+1}$ , for which we must modify  $\mathsf{sk}_{\varphi}$ . There are three key ideas in the proof, which are logically chained in an anadiplosis fashion:

- To modify  $\mathsf{sk}_{\varphi}$ , we temporarily use  $\mathsf{pad}^\mathsf{temp}$  and  $\mathfrak{s}_\mathsf{1-ABE}$  exclusively for the interaction between  $\mathsf{ct}$  and  $\mathsf{sk}_{\varphi}$ , and use  $\mathsf{pad}^\mathsf{copy}$  and  $\mathfrak{s}_\mathsf{copy}$  for the interaction between  $\mathsf{ct}$  and the other secret keys, similar to the *temporary* mode in the proof of Claim 36. With the interaction between  $\mathsf{ct}$  and  $\mathsf{sk}_{\varphi}$  isolated, we could hope to syntactically invoke 1-ABE security for them.
- To invoke 1-ABE security in  $\mathfrak{s}_{\text{1-ABE}}$ , we must make sure that in  $\mathfrak{s}_{\text{1-ABE}}$ , the ciphertext vectors use randomness independent of those in  $\mathfrak{s}_{\text{copy}}$ . This is done by invoking the DDH assumption twice in a row to make ct use  $\mathbf{r}_x$  in  $\mathsf{pad}^{\mathsf{copy}}$ ,  $\mathfrak{s}_{\mathsf{copy}}$  and independent  $\widehat{\mathbf{r}}_x$  in  $\mathsf{pad}^{\mathsf{temp}}$ ,  $\mathfrak{s}_{\text{1-ABE}}$ , similar to how the labels are simulated in the proof of Theorem 34 by invoking the DDH assumption twice in a row.
- To invoke the DDH assumption to rerandomize  $\mathbf{r}_{x}$ , there needs to be a random value multiplied to it. However, in  $\mathsf{H}_{4,\varphi}^{b}$ , nothing is multiplied to  $\mu$ 's,  $\mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{f}}$ 's,  $\widehat{\boldsymbol{\mu}}$ 's,  $\widehat{\mathbf{r}}_{\mathbf{f}}$ 's nor  $\mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}}$ . This can be resolved by a change of variable introducing a negligible statistical error:

$$(\widehat{\mu}_{\varphi}^{0}, \widehat{\mu}_{\varphi}^{1}, \widehat{\mathbf{r}}_{\varphi,f}) \longleftrightarrow (\widehat{s}\,\widehat{\mu}_{\varphi}^{0}, \widehat{s}\,\widehat{\mu}_{\varphi}^{1}, \widehat{s}\,\widehat{\mathbf{r}}_{\varphi,f}) \text{ for } \widehat{s} \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_{p}.$$

Having changed the variable, we move  $\hat{s}$  to  $\mathbf{r}_{x}$  using the function-hiding property of IPFE, after which DDH can be invoked.

We now implement these ideas in the following hybrids  $\mathsf{G}_0^\beta,\dots,\mathsf{G}_6^\beta$ :

- <u>Hybrid  $G_0^{\beta}$ </u> proceeds identically to  $H_{4,\varphi+\beta}^b$ , where the first  $\varphi-1$  secret keys have their  $\widehat{\mu}_{\varphi'}^0$  replaced by  $\widehat{\mu}_{\varphi'}^1$  in  $\mathbf{v}_{\varphi',\mathrm{pad}}[\mathsf{pad}^{\mathrm{copy}}]$ , the  $\varphi^{\mathrm{th}}$  secret key stores either  $\widehat{\mu}_{\varphi}^0$  (consistent with  $\mathbf{v}_{\varphi,\mathrm{init}}$  and  $\mathbf{v}_{\varphi,q}$ 's) or  $\widehat{\mu}_{\varphi}^1$  (inconsistent). The hybrid is shown in Figure 11.
- <u>Hybrid</u>  $\mathsf{G}_1^{\beta}$  proceeds identically to  $\mathsf{G}_0^{\beta}$ , except that a random multiplier  $\widehat{s} \overset{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_p$  is multiplied to the values at  $\mathsf{pad}^{\mathsf{copy}}$ ,  $\mathfrak{s}_{\mathsf{copy}}$  for  $\mathsf{sk}_{\varphi}$ . Conditioned on  $\widehat{s} \neq 0$  (which happens with overwhelming probability),  $\mathsf{G}_1^{\beta}$  and  $\mathsf{G}_0^{\beta}$  are identically distributed. Therefore,  $\mathsf{G}_1^{\beta} \approx_s \mathsf{G}_0^{\beta}$  taking into account the case  $\widehat{s} = 0$ .
- <u>Hybrid</u>  $G_2^{\beta}$  proceeds identically to  $G_1^{\beta}$ , except that the interaction between ct and  $\mathsf{sk}_{\varphi}$  is isolated from those between ct and the other secret keys, and that s is multiplied in ct instead of  $\mathsf{sk}_{\varphi}$ :
  - In the vectors in the  $\varphi^{th}$  secret key  $\mathsf{sk}_{\varphi}$ , values at  $\mathsf{pad}^{copy}$ ,  $\mathfrak{s}_{copy}$  are moved to  $\mathsf{pad}^{\mathsf{temp}}$ ,  $\mathfrak{s}_{1\text{-ABE}}$ , and the multiplier  $\widehat{s}$  is removed.
  - In the ciphertext vectors, values at  $pad^{copy}$ ,  $\mathfrak{s}_{copy}$  are *copied* to  $pad^{temp}$ ,  $\mathfrak{s}_{1-ABE}$ , and  $\widehat{s}$  is multiplied to the new copy.

As illustrated in Figure 11, the inner products and the public slots of the secret key vectors remain unchanged, so  $\mathsf{G}_2^\beta \approx \mathsf{G}_1^\beta$  by the function-hiding property of IPFE.

• <u>Hybrid  $G_3^{\beta}$ </u> proceeds identically to  $G_2^{\beta}$ , except that in the ciphertext vectors, the  $\hat{s}$   $\mathbf{r}_x$  in  $\mathfrak{s}_{1\text{-ABE}}$  is replaced by an independent and uniformly random  $\hat{\mathbf{s}}$ . The indistinguishability between  $G_2^{\beta}$  and  $G_3^{\beta}$  follows by the DDH assumption in  $G_1$ :

$$[\![\mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}},\widehat{s},\widehat{s}\;\mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}}]\!]_{1} \approx [\![\mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}},\widehat{s},\widehat{s}\;]\!]_{1} \text{ for } \mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{x}},\widehat{s} \xleftarrow{\$} \mathbb{Z}_{p}^{[0..T]\times[N]\times[S]\times\{0,1\}^{S}}, \widehat{s} \xleftarrow{\$} \mathbb{Z}_{p}.$$
