\mathbb{Z}_{p}^{k}, \mathbf{d} \overset{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_{p}^{k}, \mathbf{d} \overset{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_{p}^{k}, \mathbf{d} \overset{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_{p}^{k}, \mathbf{d} \overset{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_{p}^{k}, \mathbf{d} \overset{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_{p}^{k}, \mathbf{d} \overset{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_{p}^{k}, \mathbf{d} \overset{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_{p}^{k}, \mathbf{d} \overset{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_{p}^{k}, \mathbf{d} \overset{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_{p}^{k}, \mathbf{d} \overset{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_{p}^{k}, \mathbf{d} \overset{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_{p}^{k}, \mathbf{d} \overset{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_{p}^{k}, \mathbf{d} \overset{\$}{p$$

and in the second hybrid, the basis keys will have values from  $\mathbf{d}^{\mathsf{T}}$  in the private slot.

<span id="page-95-1"></span>Construction 57 (KP-ABE supporting delegation). We describe the construction for any fixed value of the security parameter  $\lambda$  and suppress the appearance of  $\lambda$  below for simplicity of notations. Let (Garble, Eval) be an AKGS for a function class  $\mathcal{F}$ ,  $\mathcal{G}$  pairing groups of order p such that MDDH<sub>k</sub> holds in  $G_2$ , and (IPFE.Setup, IPFE.KeyGen, IPFE.Enc, IPFE.Dec, IPFE.SlotEnc, IPFE.Subtract) a keyhomomorphic slotted IPFE based on  $\mathcal{G}$ . We construct an ABE scheme supporting delegation for message space  $M = G_T$ , the target group of the pairing, and the predicate space  $\mathcal{P}$  induced by  $\mathcal{F}$ :

$$X_n = \mathbb{Z}_p^n, \quad Y_n = \{ f_{\neq 0}, f_{=0} \mid f \in \mathcal{F}, f : \mathbb{Z}_p^n \to \mathbb{Z}_p \},$$
  
$$\mathcal{P} = \{ P_n : X_n \times Y_n \to \{0, 1\}, (\mathbf{x}, y) \mapsto y(\mathbf{x}) \mid n \in \mathbb{N} \}.$$

For a better exposition, we simultaneously consider two ABE schemes. The helper scheme, ( $\mathsf{Setup}_{1\text{-shot}}$ ,  $\mathsf{KeyGen}_{1\text{-shot}}$ ,  $\mathsf{Enc}$ ,  $\mathsf{Dec}$ ), supports *conjunction* with a key generation algorithm conforming to the basic ABE syntax. <sup>19</sup> The main scheme, ( $\mathsf{Setup}$ ,  $\mathsf{KeyGen}$ ,  $\mathsf{Enc}$ ,  $\mathsf{Dec}$ ), supports *delegation* and shares much of its codebase with the helper. They operate as follows:

• Setup<sub>1-shot</sub>(1<sup>n</sup>) takes the attribute length in unary (i.e.,  $P_n$  is encoded as 1<sup>n</sup>) as input. It generates IPFE master public/secret key pair (impk, imsk)  $\stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow}$  IPFE.Setup( $\mathfrak{s}_{pub}, \mathfrak{s}_{priv}$ ) for the following slots:

$$\begin{split} & \mathfrak{S}_{\mathrm{pub}} = \{\mathsf{pad}, \mathsf{const}^t, \mathsf{coef}_i^t \,|\, t \in [k], i \in [n]\}, \\ & \mathfrak{S}_{\mathrm{priv}} = \{\mathsf{const}, \mathsf{coef}_i, \mathsf{sim}_1, \mathsf{sim}_\star \,|\, i \in [n]\}. \end{split}$$

The algorithm samples  $\mathbf{B} \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_p^{k \times k}$  conditioned on  $\mathbf{B}$  being invertible and sets the basis vectors as follows:

| vector   pad                                                                                    | $const^t$               | $coef_i^t$                         | in $\mathfrak{s}_{\mathrm{priv}}$ |
|-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|-------------------------|------------------------------------|-----------------------------------|
| $\begin{array}{c c} \mathbf{b}_{const^{t'}} & 0 \\ \mathbf{b}_{coef_{i'}^{t'}} & 0 \end{array}$ | $\mathbf{B}[t,t'] \\ 0$ | $\mathbf{B}[t,t']\mathbb{1}[i=i']$ | 0                                 |

It then generates the basis keys as

$$\mathsf{bsk}_z \xleftarrow{\$} \mathsf{IPFE}.\mathsf{KeyGen}(\mathsf{imsk}, \llbracket \mathbf{b}_{\mathsf{const}^t} \rrbracket_2) \text{ for } z \in \{\mathsf{const}^t, \mathsf{coef}_i^t | i \in [n], t \in [k]\}.$$

<span id="page-95-0"></span>To keep the formalism happy, the predicates should be changed to work with  $X_n$  and  $Y_n^*$  by mapping  $(\mathbf{x}, (y_1, \ldots, y_D))$  to the conjunction of  $y_d(\mathbf{x})$ 's.

The algorithm returns  $\mathsf{mpk} = \left(\mathsf{impk}, (\mathsf{bsk}_z)_{z \in \{\mathsf{coef}^t, \mathsf{const}_i^t \mid i \in [n], t \in [k]\}}\right)$  and  $\mathsf{msk}_{1\text{-shot}} = \mathsf{imsk}$ .

Note: This procedure generates the basis keys on top of the basic ABE scheme. As far as the helper scheme (supporting conjunction without delegation) is concerned, it is not necessary to include the basis keys. It is also not harmful, and we will be able to reuse the IND-CPA security of the helper scheme for proving the IND-CPA-DLG security of the main scheme if the basis keys are included.

• KeyGen<sub>1-shot</sub>(msk<sub>1-shot</sub>,  $y_1, \ldots, y_D$ ) takes in the master secret key msk<sub>1-shot</sub> = imsk and D policies  $y_1, \ldots, y_D \in Y_n$  as input. It starts by garbling the functions underlying the policies, i.e., for all  $d \in [D]$ :

$$\boldsymbol{\mu}_d, \boldsymbol{\eta}_d \overset{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_p^k, \quad \begin{cases} \boldsymbol{\alpha}_d \leftarrow \boldsymbol{\mu}_d, \quad \boldsymbol{\beta}_d \leftarrow \boldsymbol{0}, & \text{if } y_d = f_{d, \neq 0}; \ \boldsymbol{\alpha}_d \leftarrow \boldsymbol{\eta}_d, & \text{if } y_d = f_{d, = 0}; \ \text{for } t \in [k] \colon \quad (\mathbf{L}_{d,1}^t, \dots, \mathbf{L}_{d,m_d}^t) \leftarrow \text{Garble}(f_d, \boldsymbol{\alpha}_d[t], \boldsymbol{\beta}_d[t]; \mathbf{r}_{d,t}). \end{cases}$$

The algorithm sets  $\boldsymbol{\mu} = \sum_{d=1}^{D} \boldsymbol{\mu}_d$  and assigns  $\mathbf{v}_{\text{pad}}, \mathbf{v}_{d,j}$  for  $d \in [D], j \in [m_d]$  as follows:

| vector                                       | pad                                    | $const^t$                                          | $coef_i^t$                       | in $\mathfrak{s}_{\mathrm{priv}}$ |
|----------------------------------------------|----------------------------------------|----------------------------------------------------|----------------------------------|-----------------------------------|
| $\mathbf{v}_{\text{pad}} \ \mathbf{v}_{d,j}$ | $\begin{vmatrix} 1 \\ 0 \end{vmatrix}$ | $\boldsymbol{\mu}[t] \\ \mathbf{L}_{d,j}^t[const]$ | $0 \ \mathbf{L}_{d,j}^t[coef_i]$ | 0                                 |

It generates the IPFE secret keys for those vectors and returns the secret key:

$$\begin{split} \mathsf{isk}_{\mathrm{pad}} & \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathsf{IPFE}.\mathsf{KeyGen}(\mathsf{imsk}, \llbracket \mathbf{v}_{\mathrm{pad}} \rrbracket_2), \\ \mathsf{for} \ d \in [D], j \in [m_d] \colon \ \mathsf{isk}_{d,j} & \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathsf{IPFE}.\mathsf{KeyGen}(\mathsf{imsk}, \llbracket \mathbf{v}_{d,j} \rrbracket_2), \\ \mathsf{sk}_{D:y_1,\ldots,y_D} &= (\mathsf{isk}_{\mathrm{pad}}; \ y_1, \mathsf{isk}_{1,1},\ldots, \mathsf{isk}_{1,m_1}; \ \ldots; \ y_D, \mathsf{isk}_{D,1},\ldots, \mathsf{isk}_{D,m_D}). \end{split}$$

Note:  $KeyGen_{1-shot}$  is a mixture of the basic ABE KeyGen (Construction 26) and the tweaked 1-ABE KeyGen (Appendix B.1) to support conjunctions.

• Setup(1<sup>n</sup>) takes the attribute length as input. It runs (mpk, msk<sub>1-shot</sub>)  $\stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow}$  Setup<sub>1-shot</sub>(1<sup>n</sup>) and generates the master secret key as msk = KeyGen<sub>1-shot</sub>(msk<sub>1-shot</sub>).

Note: The master secret key is simply a secret key with 0 policies (and thus pads **0**). The only component of msk is its **pad key**, which will decrypt any ict to the pad used to hide the message, giving unconditional decryption of ABE ciphertexts.

• KeyGen(mpk,  $\mathsf{sk}_{D:y_1,\dots,y_D}, y_{D+1}$ ) takes the master public key, a secret key, and a policy  $y_{D+1} \in Y_n$  as input. It parses  $\mathsf{mpk}$  as  $(\mathsf{impk}, (\mathsf{bsk}_z)_{z \in \{\mathsf{coef}^t, \mathsf{const}_i^t \mid i \in [n], t \in [k]\}})$  and

$$\mathsf{sk}_{D:y_1,\dots,y_D} \text{ as } \big(\mathsf{isk}^{\mathrm{old}}_{\mathrm{pad}}; \ y_1,\mathsf{isk}^{\mathrm{old}}_{1,1},\dots,\mathsf{isk}^{\mathrm{old}}_{1,m_1}; \ \dots; \ y_D,\mathsf{isk}^{\mathrm{old}}_{D,1},\dots,\mathsf{isk}^{\mathrm{old}}_{D,m_D} \big).$$

The algorithm generates fresh garblings for all the D+1 policies, i.e., for all  $d \in [D+1]$ :

$$\boldsymbol{\mu}_d^{\text{new}}, \boldsymbol{\eta}_d^{\text{new}} \overset{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_p^k, \quad \begin{cases} \boldsymbol{\alpha}_d^{\text{new}} \leftarrow \boldsymbol{\mu}_d^{\text{new}}, & \boldsymbol{\beta}_d^{\text{new}} \leftarrow \boldsymbol{0}, & \text{if } y_d = f_{d, \neq 0}; \ \boldsymbol{\alpha}_d^{\text{new}} \leftarrow \boldsymbol{\eta}_d^{\text{new}}, & \text{if } y_d = f_{d, \neq 0}; \ & \text{for } t \in [k] \colon \ (\mathbf{L}_{d,1}^{t, \text{new}}, \dots, \mathbf{L}_{d,m_d}^{t, \text{new}}) \leftarrow \mathsf{Garble}(f_d, \boldsymbol{\alpha}_d^{\text{new}}[t], \boldsymbol{\beta}_d^{\text{new}}[t]; \mathbf{r}_{d,t}^{\text{new}}). \end{cases}$$

It then uses IPFE key-homomorphism to combine the old and new label functions as well as the pads, forming the delegated key:

$$\begin{aligned} \mathsf{isk}_{\mathrm{pad}} & \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathsf{isk}_{\mathrm{pad}}^{\mathrm{old}} + \sum_{t=1}^{k} \boldsymbol{\mu}^{\mathrm{new}}[t] \mathsf{bsk}_{\mathsf{const}^t}, \, \mathsf{where} \,\, \boldsymbol{\mu}^{\mathrm{new}} \leftarrow \sum_{d=1}^{D+1} \boldsymbol{\mu}_{d}^{\mathrm{new}}, \\ \mathsf{for} \,\, d \in [D+1], j \in [m_d] \colon & \mathsf{isk}_{d,j}^{\mathrm{new}} & \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \sum_{t=1}^{k} \left( \mathbf{L}_{d,j}^{t,\mathrm{new}}[\mathsf{const}] \mathsf{bsk}_{\mathsf{const}^t} + \sum_{i=1}^{n} \mathbf{L}_{d,j}^{t,\mathrm{new}}[\mathsf{coef}_i] \mathsf{bsk}_{\mathsf{coef}_i^t} \right), \\ & \mathsf{isk}_{d,j} & \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \begin{cases} \mathsf{isk}_{d,j}^{\mathrm{old}} + \mathsf{isk}_{d,j}^{\mathrm{new}}, & \mathsf{if} \,\, d \in [D]; \\ \mathsf{isk}_{D+1,j}^{\mathrm{new}}, & \mathsf{if} \,\, d = D+1; \end{cases} \\ \mathsf{sk}_{D+1:y_1,\ldots,y_{D+1}} & = \left(\mathsf{isk}_{\mathrm{pad}}; \,\, y_1, \mathsf{isk}_{1,1}, \ldots, \mathsf{isk}_{1,m_1}; \,\, \ldots; \,\, y_{D+1}, \mathsf{isk}_{D+1,1}, \ldots, \mathsf{isk}_{D+1,m_{D+1}} \right). \end{aligned}$$

Note: We will show (Lemma 58) that the secret key output by KeyGen is identically distributed to one by KeyGen<sub>1-shot</sub> for the same list of policies, provided that the input secret key is well-formed.

• Enc(mpk,  $\mathbf{x}, g$ ) takes the master public key mpk = (impk,...), the attribute  $\mathbf{x} \in X_n = \mathbb{Z}_p^n$ , and the message  $g \in G_T$  as input. It generates the ciphertext in the same way as the basic ABE construction. The algorithm samples  $\mathbf{s} \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_p^k$  and sets  $\mathbf{u}$  as follows:

| vector | pad | $const^t$       | $coef_i^t$                   |
|--------|-----|-----------------|------------------------------|
| u      | h   | $\mathbf{s}[t]$ | $\mathbf{s}[t]\mathbf{x}[i]$ |

It returns the following ciphertext:

$$\mathsf{ict} \overset{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathsf{IPFE}.\mathsf{SlotEnc}(\mathsf{impk}, \llbracket \mathbf{u} \rrbracket_1), \quad \mathsf{ct} = (\llbracket h \rrbracket_{\mathsf{T}} + g, \mathbf{x}, \mathsf{ict}).$$

• Dec(sk, ct) parses ct as ( $[\![z]\!]_T$ ,  $\mathbf{x}$ , ict) and sk as (isk<sub>pad</sub>;  $y_1$ , isk<sub>1,1</sub>,..., isk<sub>1,m1</sub>; ...;  $y_D$ , isk<sub>D,1</sub>,..., isk<sub>D,mD</sub>). It returns  $\bot$  if  $y_d(\mathbf{x}) = 0$  for some  $d \in [D]$ . Otherwise, it does the following:

$$\begin{split} & & \quad \|z'\|_{\mathrm{T}} \leftarrow \mathsf{IPFE.Dec}(\mathsf{isk}_{\mathrm{pad}},\mathsf{ict}), \\ \text{for } d \in [D], j \in [m_d] \colon & \quad \|\ell_{d,j}\|_{\mathrm{T}} \leftarrow \mathsf{IPFE.Dec}(\mathsf{isk}_{d,j},\mathsf{ict}), \\ & \quad \|\mu_d'\|_{\mathrm{T}} \leftarrow \begin{cases} \frac{1}{f_d(\mathbf{x})} \mathsf{Eval}(f_d,\mathbf{x},[\![\ell_{d,1}]\!]_{\mathrm{T}},\dots,[\![\ell_{d,m_d}]\!]_{\mathrm{T}}), & \text{if } y_d = f_{d,\neq 0}; \\ & \quad \mathsf{Eval}(f_d,\mathbf{x},[\![\ell_{d,1}]\!]_{\mathrm{T}},\dots,[\![\ell_{d,m_d}]\!]_{\mathrm{T}}), & \text{if } y_d = f_{d,=0}. \end{cases} \end{split}$$

The algorithm returns  $[\![z]\!]_{\mathrm{T}} + \sum_{d=1}^D [\![\mu'_d]\!]_{\mathrm{T}} - [\![z']\!]_{\mathrm{T}}$  as the decrypted message.

Note: By generalizing the argument for the correctness of the basic ABE scheme (Construction 26) in the same way as for the tweaked 1-ABE scheme, we know that Dec correctly recovers the message in the scheme (Setup<sub>1-shot</sub>, KeyGen<sub>1-shot</sub>, Enc, Dec). Once we show the equivalence between KeyGen<sub>1-shot</sub> and KeyGen, we obtain the correctness of (Setup, KeyGen, Enc, Dec).

<span id="page-98-0"></span>**Lemma 58.** Suppose in Construction 57, the IPFE scheme is perfectly key-homomorphic, then for all  $\lambda \in \mathbb{N}$ ,  $n \in \mathbb{N}$ ,  $D \in \mathbb{N}$  and all  $y_1, \ldots, y_D, y_{D+1} \in Y_{\lambda,n}$ , the following distributions are identical:

$$\begin{cases} (\mathsf{mpk}, \mathsf{msk}_{1\text{-}\mathrm{shot}}) \xleftarrow{\$} \mathsf{Setup}_{1\text{-}\mathrm{shot}}(1^{\lambda}, 1^n) \\ \mathsf{sk}_D \xleftarrow{\$} \mathsf{KeyGen}_{1\text{-}\mathrm{shot}}(\mathsf{msk}_{1\text{-}\mathrm{shot}}, y_1, \dots, y_D) & : (\mathsf{mpk}, \mathsf{msk}_{1\text{-}\mathrm{shot}}, \mathsf{sk}_D, \mathsf{sk}_{D+1}) \\ \mathsf{sk}_{D+1} \xleftarrow{\$} \mathsf{KeyGen}_{1\text{-}\mathrm{shot}}(\mathsf{msk}_{1\text{-}\mathrm{shot}}, y_1, \dots, y_D, y_{D+1}) \\ \end{cases} \\ \begin{cases} (\mathsf{mpk}, \mathsf{msk}_{1\text{-}\mathrm{shot}}) \xleftarrow{\$} \mathsf{Setup}_{1\text{-}\mathrm{shot}}(1^{\lambda}, 1^n) \\ \mathsf{sk}_D \xleftarrow{\$} \mathsf{KeyGen}_{1\text{-}\mathrm{shot}}(\mathsf{msk}_{1\text{-}\mathrm{shot}}, y_1, \dots, y_D) \\ \mathsf{sk}_{D+1} \xleftarrow{\$} \mathsf{KeyGen}(\mathsf{mpk}, \mathsf{sk}_D, y_{D+1}) \end{cases} \\ \vdots (\mathsf{mpk}, \mathsf{msk}_{1\text{-}\mathrm{shot}}, \mathsf{sk}_D, \mathsf{sk}_D, \mathsf{sk}_{D+1}) \end{cases}$$

<u>Proof (sketch).</u> Recall that KeyGen creates new garblings, and uses key-homomorphism and the basis keys to combine the new garblings into the old keys. Since key-homomorphism is perfect and every old key takes part in *some* operation to form the new key, it suffices to show that the vectors encrypted in the keys in  $\mathsf{sk}_{D+1}$  follows the same distribution in the two cases.

Combining the linearity of Garble,  $\mathbf{B}$  being invertible, and the fact that KeyGen generates fresh garblings for all the policies and combines the newly generated one (with a change of basis determined by  $\mathbf{B}$ ) with the old ones (which are *valid* garblings), the vectors encrypted in  $\mathsf{sk}_{D+1}$  generated by KeyGen encode independently generated garblings for independently sampled pads, which are the same as the ones created using  $\mathsf{KeyGen}_{1\text{-shot}}$ . The verification is easy in principle but tedious to practice. We omit it here.

<span id="page-98-1"></span>**Lemma 59.** Suppose in Construction 57, the AKGS is piecewise secure, the  $\mathrm{MDDH}_k$  assumption holds in  $G_2$ , and the slotted IPFE is function-hiding, then the helper scheme (Setup\_1-shot, KeyGen\_1-shot, Enc, Dec) is IND-CPA secure.

<u>Proof (sketch).</u> The proof is similar to that of Theorem 27 (IND-CPA of the basic ABE), except that we need one extra preparation step and have to take care of the basis keys. We highlight them and leave the rest to the reader.

Recall that in  $\mathsf{Exp}_{\mathsf{CPA}}^b$ , the adversary receives  $\mathsf{mpk}$  (consisting of  $\mathsf{impk}$  and  $\mathsf{bsk}_z$ 's),  $\mathsf{sk}_q$  for the conjunction of  $y_{q,1},\ldots,y_{q,D_q}$ , and  $\mathsf{ct}$  encrypting  $g_b$  under attribute  $\mathbf{x}$ , where  $y_{1,1},\ldots,y_{1,D_1};\ldots;y_{Q,1},\ldots,y_{Q,D_Q}$  and  $g_0,g_1,\mathbf{x}$  are chosen adaptively by  $\mathcal{A}$  subject to the constraint that each queried key should not decrypt the ciphertext, i.e., for all  $q \in [Q]$ , there exists  $d_q \in [D_q]$  such that  $y_{q,d_q}(\mathbf{x}) = 0$ . The basis keys  $\mathsf{bsk}_z$ 's encrypt a basis determined by a random invertible matrix  $\mathbf{B}$  for the indices  $\mathsf{const}^t$ ,  $\mathsf{coef}_i^t$ . The adversary needs to distinguish the two cases.

As before, the proof goes by moving the computation of the garblings for the challenge ciphertext to the private slot, invoking  $\mathrm{MDDH}_k$  to argue the garblings in the private slot are indistinguishable from independently generated garblings for independently sampled pads, and lastly reducing IND-CPA security to 1-ABE security.

We describe the *first few* hybrids (the indices are aligned with those in the proof of Theorem 27):

- <u>Hybrid H</u><sup>b</sup><sub>0</sub> proceeds identically to  $\mathsf{Exp}^b_{\mathsf{CPA}}$ . As shown in Figure 13, ict in the challenge ciphertext is generated using  $\mathsf{IPFE}.\mathsf{SlotEnc}$  (with  $\bot$  values in the private slot), the basis keys  $\mathsf{bsk}_z$  and the secret keys  $\mathsf{sk}_q$  are generated normally.
- <u>Hybrid H</u><sup>b</sup><sub>1</sub> proceeds identically to H<sup>b</sup><sub>0</sub>, except that the IPFE ciphertext in the challenge ciphertext is generated using IPFE.Enc with 0 values in the private slot. By the slot-mode correctness, we have H<sup>b</sup><sub>0</sub>  $\equiv$  H<sup>b</sup><sub>1</sub>.

<span id="page-99-0"></span>

| hybrid                              | vector                                                                    | pad                                    | $const^t$                                             | $coef_i^t$                                 | const                                                                        | $coef_i  sim_1$                                                            | $, sim_\star$ |
|-------------------------------------|---------------------------------------------------------------------------|----------------------------------------|-------------------------------------------------------|--------------------------------------------|------------------------------------------------------------------------------|----------------------------------------------------------------------------|---------------|
| $H_0^b \equiv Exp_{\mathrm{CPA}}^b$ | $\begin{array}{c c} bsk_{const^{t'}} \\ bsk_{coef_{i'}^{t'}} \end{array}$ | $\begin{bmatrix} 0 \\ 0 \end{bmatrix}$ | $\mathbf{B}[t,t'] \\ 0$                               | $0\\ \mathbf{B}[t,t']\mathbb{1}[i=i']$     | 0 0                                                                          | 0                                                                          | 0             |
|                                     |                                                                           | $\begin{vmatrix} 1 \\ 0 \end{vmatrix}$ | $\boldsymbol{\mu}_q[t] \ \mathbf{L}_{q,d,i}^t[const]$ | $\mathbf{L}_{q,d,j}^{t}[coef_i]$           | 0 0                                                                          | 0<br>0                                                                     | $0 \\ 0$      |
|                                     | $\begin{bmatrix} \bar{ct} \end{bmatrix}$ : <b>u</b>                       | h                                      | $\mathbf{s}[t]$                                       | $\mathbf{s}[t]\mathbf{x}[i]$               | 上                                                                            | $\perp$                                                                    | Τ             |
|                                     | $bsk_{const^{t'}}$                                                        | 0                                      | $\mathbf{B}[t,t']$                                    | 0                                          |                                                                              | 0                                                                          | 0             |
|                                     | $bsk_{coef_{i'}^{t'}}$                                                    | 0                                      | 0                                                     | $\mathbf{B}[t,t']\mathbb{1}[i=i']$         | 0                                                                            | $\begin{bmatrix} 0 \end{bmatrix}$                                          | 0             |
| $H_1^b$                             | $sk_q \colon \mathbf{v}_{q,\mathrm{pad}}$                                 | 1                                      | $\boldsymbol{\mu}_q[t]$                               | 0                                          | $\begin{bmatrix} 0 \end{bmatrix}$                                            | 0                                                                          | 0             |
|                                     | $sk_q \colon \mathbf{v}_{q,d,j}$                                          | 0                                      | $\mathbf{L}_{q,d,j}^{t}[const]$                       | $\mathbf{L}_{q,d,j}^t[coef_i]$             | $\begin{bmatrix} 0 \end{bmatrix}$                                            | $\begin{bmatrix} 0 \end{bmatrix}$                                          | 0             |
|                                     | ct: u                                                                     | h                                      | $[\mathbf{s}[t]]$                                     | $\mathbf{s}[t]\mathbf{x}[i]$               | $\begin{bmatrix} 0 \end{bmatrix}$                                            | $\begin{bmatrix} 0 \end{bmatrix}$                                          | 0             |
|                                     | $bsk_{const^{t'}}$                                                        | 0                                      | $\left[\mathbf{B}[t,t']\right]$                       | 0                                          | $\boxed{ (\mathbf{B}^{\scriptscriptstyleT}\mathbf{s})[t'] }$                 | 0                                                                          | 0             |
|                                     | $bsk_{coef_{i'}^{t'}}$                                                    | 0                                      | 0                                                     | $\mathbf{B}[t,t']\mathbb{1}[i=i']$         | 0                                                                            | $\boxed{(\mathbf{B}^{\scriptscriptstyleT}\mathbf{s})[t']\mathbb{1}[i=i']}$ | 0             |
| $H_2^b$                             | $sk_q \colon \mathbf{v}_{q,\mathrm{pad}}$                                 | 1                                      | $\boldsymbol{\mu}_q[t]$                               | 0                                          | $\boxed{\overline{\mu}_q}$                                                   | 0                                                                          | 0             |
|                                     | $\boxed{sk_q \colon \mathbf{v}_{q,d,j}}$                                  | 0                                      | $\mathbf{L}_{q,d,j}^{t}[const]$                       | $\mathbf{L}_{q,d,j}^t[coef_i]$             | $\overline{\mathbf{L}}_{q,d,j}[const]$                                       | $\boxed{\overline{\mathbf{L}}_{q,d,j}[coef_i]}$                            | 0             |
|                                     | ct: u                                                                     | h                                      | 0                                                     | 0                                          | 1                                                                            | $\boxed{\mathbf{x}[i]}$                                                    | 0             |
|                                     | $bsk_{const^{t'}}$                                                        | 0                                      | $\mathbf{B}[t,t']$                                    | 0                                          | $\boxed{(\mathbf{B}^{\scriptscriptstyleT}\mathbf{s})[t']}$                   | 0                                                                          | 0             |
|                                     | $bsk_{coef_{i'}^{t'}}$                                                    | 0                                      | 0                                                     | $\boxed{\mathbf{B}[t,t']\mathbb{1}[i=i']}$ | 0                                                                            | $\boxed{(\mathbf{B}^{\scriptscriptstyleT}\mathbf{s})[t']\mathbb{1}[i=i']}$ | 0             |
| H <sup>b</sup> <sub>2.71828</sub>   | $sk_q \colon \mathbf{v}_{q,\mathrm{pad}}$                                 | 1                                      | $\boldsymbol{\mu}_q[t]$                               | 0                                          | $\boxed{\bar{\overline{\mu}_q}}$                                             | 0                                                                          | 0             |
|                                     | $sk_q \colon \mathbf{v}_{q,d,j}$                                          |                                        | $\mathbf{L}_{q,d,j}^{t}[const]$                       | $\mathbf{L}_{q,d,j}^t[coef_i]$             | $\left \lceil \overline{\overline{\mathbf{L}}}_{q,d,j}[const] \right \rceil$ | L                                                                          | 0             |
|                                     | ct: u                                                                     | $\frac{\mid h \mid}{\mid}$             | 0                                                     | 0                                          | 1                                                                            | $\mathbf{x}[i]$                                                            | 0             |
| $H_3^b$                             | $bsk_{const^{t'}}$                                                        | 0                                      | $\mathbf{B}[t,t']$                                    | 0                                          | $\boxed{\mathbf{d}[t']}$                                                     | 0                                                                          | 0             |
|                                     | $bsk_{coef_{i'}^{t'}}$                                                    | 0                                      | 0                                                     | $\mathbf{B}[t,t']\mathbb{1}[i=i']$         | 0                                                                            | $\boxed{\mathbf{d}[t']\mathbb{1}[i=i']}$                                   | 0             |
|                                     | $sk_q \colon \mathbf{v}_{q,\mathrm{pad}}$                                 | 1                                      | $\boldsymbol{\mu}_q[t]$                               | 0                                          | $\left[\widehat{\mu}_{q}\right]$                                             | 0                                                                          | 0             |
|                                     | $ $ sk $_q$ : $\mathbf{v}_{q,d,j}$                                        | 1                                      |                                                       | $\mathbf{L}_{q,d,j}^t[coef_i]$             | $\widehat{\mathbf{L}}_{q,d,j}[const]$                                        | $\boxed{\widehat{\mathbf{L}}_{q,d,j}[coef_i]}$                             | 0             |
|                                     | ct: u                                                                     | $\mid h \mid$                          | 0                                                     | 0                                          | 1                                                                            | $\mathbf{x}[i]$                                                            | 0             |

The hybrids are illustrated with ciphertext challenge coming after the key queries (as in the more difficult case for 1-ABE). In reality, the key queries can be made before and after the ciphertext challenge, and the proof is unaffected.

In  $\mathsf{H}_2^b$ , the linearly combined  $\overset{\smile}{\mathbf{L}}_{q,j}^- = \sum_{t \in [k]} \mathbf{s}[t] \mathbf{L}_{q,j}^t$  are valid garblings for  $\overline{\mu}_q = \langle \mathbf{s}, \boldsymbol{\mu}_q \rangle$ . In  $\mathsf{H}_{2.71828...}^b$ ,  $\mathsf{H}_3^b$ , the matrix  $\mathbf{B}$  is uniformly random (not conditioned on being invertible). In  $\mathsf{H}_3^b$ , the garblings  $\hat{\mathbf{L}}_{q,j}$  are fresh and are for freshly sampled pads  $\hat{\mu}_q$ .

Figure 13: The first few hybrids the proof of IND-CPA security of (Setup<sub>1-shot</sub>, KeyGen<sub>1-shot</sub>, Enc, Dec) in Construction 57 (cf. Figure 4).

• <u>Hybrid  $H_2^b$ </u> proceeds identically to  $H_1^b$ , except that we hardwire the linear combination coefficients s into the IPFE keys. We refer the readers to the proof of Theorem 27 for the handling of the ABE secret keys and the challenge ciphertext, and focus on the basis keys. In  $H_1^b$ , the inner product between the vector in the basis key  $bsk_{const}t'$  and the challenge ciphertext was

$$\sum_{t=1}^k \mathbf{B}[t,t']\mathbf{s}[t] = \sum_{t=1}^k \mathbf{B}^\mathsf{T}[t',t]\mathbf{s}[t] = (\mathbf{B}^\mathsf{T}\mathbf{s})[t'].$$

So it suffices to put  $(\mathbf{B}^\mathsf{T}\mathbf{s})[t']$  at index const of the vector in  $\mathsf{bsk}_{\mathsf{const}^{t'}}$ . Similarly, in  $\mathsf{bsk}_{\mathsf{coef}_{i'}^{t'}}$ , we should embed  $(\mathbf{B}^\mathsf{T}\mathbf{s})[t']$  at index  $\mathsf{coef}_{i'}$  to keep the inner product unchanged, as depicted in Figure 13. Since we make sure the inner products do not change,  $\mathsf{H}_1^b \approx \mathsf{H}_2^b$  by the function-hiding property.

- <u>Hybrid  $H_{2.71828...}^b$ </u> proceeds identically to  $H_2^b$ , except that we do not condition **B** on being invertible. This step does not appear in the proof for the basic ABE, and is a preparation step for invoking MDDH<sub>k</sub>. A random square matrix over  $\mathbb{Z}_p$  is invertible with overwhelming probability, so  $H_2^b \approx_s H_{2.71828...}^b$ .
- <u>Hybrid H</u><sup>b</sup><sub>3</sub> proceeds identically to H<sup>b</sup><sub>2.71828...</sub>, except that in the private slot of the secret keys, the garblings are generated independent of the public slot garblings and for freshly sampled pads, and that in the private slot of the basis keys,  $\mathbf{B}^{\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{s}$  is replaced by  $\mathbf{d} \stackrel{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_p^k$ . Similar to the proof of Theorem 27, we rely on the MDDH<sub>k</sub> assumption in  $G_2$  (IPFE secret key encoding group) to argue H<sup>b</sup><sub>2.71828...</sub>  $\approx$  H<sup>b</sup><sub>3</sub>. The only difference is that we invoke MDDH<sub>k,N+k</sub> instead of MDDH<sub>k,N</sub>, where N is the total number of random elements used in the public slot garblings. The MDDH<sub>k</sub> assumption implies

$$[\![\mathbf{A},\mathbf{B},\mathbf{s}^{\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{A},\mathbf{s}^{\mathsf{T}}\mathbf{B}]\!]_{2} \approx [\![\mathbf{A},\mathbf{B},\mathbf{c}^{\mathsf{T}},\mathbf{d}^{\mathsf{T}}]\!]_{2} \quad \text{for} \quad \mathbf{A} \overset{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_{p}^{k\times N}, \mathbf{B} \overset{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_{p}^{k\times k}, \mathbf{s} \overset{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_{p}^{k}, \mathbf{c} \overset{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_{p}^{N}, \mathbf{d} \overset{\$}{\leftarrow} \mathbb{Z}_{p}^{k}.$$

Given  $\mathbf{A}, \mathbf{B}$  and  $\mathbf{c}^{\mathsf{T}}, \mathbf{d}^{\mathsf{T}}$  that are either  $\mathbf{s}^{\mathsf{T}} \mathbf{A}, \mathbf{s}^{\mathsf{T}} \mathbf{B}$  or random, we use  $\mathbf{B}, \mathbf{d}$  to form the public/private slots of the basis keys, and  $\mathbf{A}, \mathbf{c}$  as the randomness of the garblings in the public/private slots of the queried secret keys. The latter part is again attributed to the linearity of AKGS Garble. If  $\mathbf{c}^{\mathsf{T}}, \mathbf{d}^{\mathsf{T}}$  are sampled as  $\mathbf{s}^{\mathsf{T}} \mathbf{A}, \mathbf{s}^{\mathsf{T}} \mathbf{B}$ , the created keys follow the distribution specified in  $\mathsf{H}_{2.71828...}^b$ ; otherwise, the distribution is that specified in  $\mathsf{H}_3^b$ . Therefore,  $\mathsf{H}_{2.71828...}^b \approx \mathsf{H}_3^b$  by the MDDH<sub>k</sub> assumption in  $G_2$ .

The proof then proceeds the same as that of Theorem 27, and we omit the rest.

Corollary 60. Suppose in Construction 57, the AKGS is piecewise secure, the  $MDDH_k$  assumption holds in  $G_2$ , and the slotted IPFE is function-hiding and perfectly key-homomorphic, then the main scheme (Setup, KeyGen, Enc, Dec) is IND-CPA-DLG secure.

<u>Proof (sketch).</u> We prove the corollary by reduction to the IND-CPA security of the helper scheme. Recall that in the IND-CPA-DLG experiments, the adversary  $\mathcal{A}$  can delegate and reveal secret keys, and request a ciphertext encrypting one of the two messages under some attribute. The policies to delegate, the secret keys to reveal, the messages and the attribute are chosen adaptively by  $\mathcal{A}$ , subject to the constraint that any revealed key has some policy that disallows the challenge attribute. The task of  $\mathcal{A}$  is to tell which message is being encrypted.

By Lemma 58 (and a hybrid argument over D), instead of delegating the secret keys (from msk and other delegated keys) and revealing them as requested, it is identical to remember the policies

for the would-be-delegated keys and generate the secret key using KeyGen1-shot and msk1-shot when it is requested for revelation for the first time. With this change made, the IND-CPA-DLG security experiments of the main scheme is exactly the IND-CPA security experiments of the helper scheme (plus some bookkeeping), and we conclude security by Lemma [59.](#page-98-1)

# <span id="page-101-0"></span>C Proof of Theorem [20](#page-27-3)

Proof. Suppose (Garble, Eval) is a piecewise secure AKGS.

We first show that `<sup>1</sup> has non-zero coefficient in Eval. Consider a function f : Z n <sup>p</sup> → Z<sup>p</sup> of garbling size m. By Lemma [17,](#page-26-0) for any α, β, the labels for a garbling of f with secrets α, β can be simulated as `2, . . . , `<sup>m</sup> \$← Z<sup>p</sup> and `<sup>1</sup> \$← RevSamp(f, x, γ, `2, . . . , `m). In particular, `<sup>2</sup> = · · · = `<sup>m</sup> = 0 is a possible assignment of the labels for α = 0, β = 1 with positive probability. By the (perfect) correctness, for this assignment, we have

$$1 = \ell_1 \mathsf{Eval}(f, \mathbf{x}, 1, 0, \dots, 0) \quad \Longrightarrow \quad \mathsf{Eval}(f, \mathbf{x}, 1, 0, \dots, 0) \neq 0.$$

Now we show how to find the change of variable for the randomness to write the labels in the special form with randomizers. Let r be the randomness used by Garble and L1, . . . ,L<sup>m</sup> the coefficients of the label functions as functions of α, β, r. By the linearity requirement,

$$\mathbf{L}_{j}[z] = u_{j,z}\alpha + v_{j,z}\beta + \langle \mathbf{w}_{j,z}, \mathbf{r} \rangle$$

for some uj,z, vj,z, wj,z determined by f. Consider the following process that computes a basis B for the dual space of r:

$$\mathcal{B} \leftarrow \varnothing$$
for  $j = m, m - 1, m - 2, \dots, 2$ :
for  $i = 1, \dots, n$ :\nif  $\mathbf{w}_{j, \mathsf{coef}_i}$  is linearly independent of  $\mathcal{B}$ :
 $\mathcal{B} \leftarrow \mathcal{B} \cup \{\mathbf{w}_{j, \mathsf{coef}_i}\}$ 
 $\mathcal{B} \leftarrow \mathcal{B} \cup \{\mathbf{w}_{j, \mathsf{const}}\}$ 
complete  $\mathcal{B}$  into a basis if it is not yet a basis

We claim that B is always a linearly independent set. Clearly, initially B = ∅ is linearly independent. By how we add wj,coef<sup>i</sup> 's, none of these steps change B from being linearly independent to being linearly dependent. Consider each time we add some w<sup>j</sup> <sup>∗</sup>,const and suppose (for the sake of contradiction) that w<sup>j</sup> <sup>∗</sup>,const were already in the span of B by the time we add it, then we would have

$$\mathbf{w}_{j^*,\mathsf{const}} = \sum_{i=1}^n a_i \mathbf{w}_{j^*,\mathsf{coef}_i} + \sum_{j>j^*,z} b_{j,z} \mathbf{w}_{j,z} \quad \text{for some } a_i,b_{j,z} \in \mathbb{Z}_p.$$

Now consider garbling f with secrets α = β = 0 and setting x[i] = −a<sup>i</sup> . Given L<sup>j</sup> <sup>∗</sup>+1, . . . ,Lm, the label `<sup>j</sup> <sup>∗</sup> would be determined, contradicting the marginal randomness property:

$$\ell_{j^*} = \sum_{i=1}^n \mathbf{x}[i] \langle \mathbf{w}_{j^*, \mathsf{coef}_i}, \mathbf{r} \rangle + \sum_{i=1}^n a_i \langle \mathbf{w}_{j^*, \mathsf{coef}_i}, \mathbf{r} \rangle + \sum_{j>j^*, z} b_{j,z} \langle \mathbf{w}_{j^*, z}, \mathbf{r} \rangle$$
$$= \sum_{j>j^*, z} b_{j,z} \mathbf{L}_j[z] \qquad (\text{since } \mathbf{x}[i] + a_i = 0).$$

Therefore, no step of adding  $\mathbf{w}_{j,\mathsf{const}}$  makes  $\mathcal{B}$  linearly dependent.

Given the basis  $\mathcal{B} = \{\mathbf{b}_t, \dots, \mathbf{b}_1\}$  (with  $\mathbf{b}_t$  being the first vector added to  $\mathcal{B}$ ), we change the randomness to be  $\tilde{\mathbf{r}}$  for  $\tilde{\mathbf{r}}[t] = \langle \mathbf{b}_t, \mathbf{r} \rangle$ , which amounts to a change of basis of  $\mathbf{r}$  (to the dual basis of  $\mathcal{B}$ ). Note that since  $\mathcal{B}$  is efficiently computable, so is the bijection between  $\mathbf{r}$  and  $\tilde{\mathbf{r}}$ . The garbling scheme now uses  $\tilde{\mathbf{r}}$  as the randomness, and garbles by first computing  $\mathbf{r}$  then using the underlying procedure with  $\mathbf{r}$ .

For all j > 1, the label function  $L_j(\mathbf{x})$  is in the special form with randomizer  $\tilde{\mathbf{r}}[t_j]$  for some  $t_j$  —  $\tilde{\mathbf{r}}[t_j] = \langle \mathbf{w}_{j,\mathsf{const}}, \mathbf{r} \rangle$  appears in the constant term as  $+\tilde{\mathbf{r}}[t_j]$ , the non-constant coefficients and the coefficients of any label function  $\mathbf{L}_{j'}$  with j' > j only use  $\tilde{\mathbf{r}}[t]$  with  $t > t_j$ .
